FOREWORD  By THE EXECUTIVE  DIRECTOR  | 7

--- Document Chunk 291 ---
Foreword by the 

--- Document Chunk 292 ---
Executive Director

--- Document Chunk 293 ---
2024 marks the 20th anniversary of the creation of the European Union Agency for 

--- Document Chunk 294 ---
Railways. Since its foundation, ERA has been at the side of the European railway stake -

--- Document Chunk 295 ---
holders, carrying out an ever-increasing set of crucial tasks for railways. I am proud of all 

--- Document Chunk 296 ---
the achievements the Agency has accomplished during the last 20 years and I am con -

--- Document Chunk 297 ---
fident the Agency will bring even more added value to the railway sector in the future, 

--- Document Chunk 298 ---
especially with the progressive development of the Single European Railways Area.

--- Document Chunk 299 ---
In the recent years, we have witnessed many worrying trends, such as the resurgence of 

--- Document Chunk 300 ---
war on the European continent, certain macroeconomic challenges, as well as increasing-

--- Document Chunk 301 ---
ly serious climate change impacts across the world. In such worrying environment, trans-

--- Document Chunk 302 ---
port has a crucial role to play, not only in ensuring the safe transport of people and goods, 

--- Document Chunk 303 ---
but as well in the decarbonisation of the sector and its adaptability to a changing climate. 

--- Document Chunk 304 ---
Safety is also a crucial element for railways. Following the tragic rail accident which took 

--- Document Chunk 305 ---
place in February 2023 near Larissa in Greece, we need to ensure that the right measures 

--- Document Chunk 306 ---
and checks are put in place to prevent such accidents from happening again. “A sustain -

--- Document Chunk 307 ---
able, safe European transport system without frontiers” does therefore not only represent 

--- Document Chunk 308 ---
our Agency’s vision statement, but also reflects the ambition of the rail sector at large.

--- Document Chunk 309 ---
In line with its mandate, the European Union Agency for Railways aims at covering a wide 

--- Document Chunk 310 ---
range of areas of work, involving actions to drive the continuation of the progress with 

--- Document Chunk 311 ---
railway safety and interoperability, together with its role of EU-wide authority for Vehicle 

--- Document Chunk 312 ---
Authorisation, Single Safety Certification, and ERTMS Trackside Approval.

--- Document Chunk 313 ---
The multi-annual work programme 2024-2026, together with the annual programme 

--- Document Chunk 314 ---
2024 have been planned and prepared following the principles of the intervention log-

--- Document Chunk 315 ---
ic. In addition, the work programme was prepared reflecting the conclusions of the SPD 

--- Document Chunk 316 ---
2024 Workshop held with the Management Board in June 2022.

--- Document Chunk 317 ---
The year 2024 will be an important milestone for our Authority activities, as also it marks 

--- Document Chunk 318 ---
the fifth year since the start of the Agency’s Authority activities according to the technical 

--- Document Chunk 319 ---
pillar of the 4

--- Document Chunk 320 ---
th Railway Package. The Agency has now gained significant experience in 

--- Document Chunk 321 ---
running the tasks related to its Authority role, as well as in forecasting their volume to the 

--- Document Chunk 322 ---
best extent possible, considering the challenges of a moving macroeconomic context. 

--- Document Chunk 323 ---
However, the volatility of the applications and their volumes can still greatly differ from 

--- Document Chunk 324 ---
one year to the other, which renders the planning of activities and the detailed forecast 

--- Document Chunk 325 ---
of revenues somewhat complex. The Agency will continue to monitor this aspect closely 

--- Document Chunk 326 ---
and to apply its agile management of these tasks. In addition, it is important to note that 

--- Document Chunk 327 ---
the Agency has reached an increasingly higher maturity level with the processing of au -

--- Document Chunk 328 ---
thorisation and certification tasks, which provides for a higher efficiency in their delivery.

--- Document Chunk 329 ---
The Agency will also continue to reinforce its efficiency and effectiveness for this multian-

--- Document Chunk 330 ---
nual work programme. In 2022 already, the Agency’s Management Board adopted the 

--- Document Chunk 331 ---
Strengthening Plan and its subsequent action plan prepared by the Agency in close 

--- Document Chunk 332 ---
cooperation with the European Commission, highlighting the critical importance of ar -

--- Document Chunk 333 ---
eas of works such as: TSIs and national rules clean up, ERTMS, CSM ASLP , the monitoring 

--- Document Chunk 334 ---
of NSAs and NoBos, as well as data and digitalization. As a result, the Agency received 

--- Document Chunk 335 ---
an increase of 12 temporary agent posts (TAs) starting in 2023, which should be entirely 

--- Document Chunk 336 ---
covered through the Agency’s existing stream of revenues. The latter represents a signif-

--- Document Chunk 337 ---
icant challenge, especially in the context of a volatile pattern of inflation. Continuously, 

--- Document Chunk 338 ---
the Agency is making a thorough assessment of its capacity to cover these costs in a 

--- Document Chunk 339 ---
Josef Doppelbauer

--- Document Chunk 340 ---
8 | SINGLE PROGRAMMING DOCUMENT 2024-2026

--- Document Chunk 341 ---
sustainable manner until the end of MFF 2021-2027. Additionally,  the Agency is making 

--- Document Chunk 342 ---
sustained efforts for a combined response to the resourcing challenge by increasing the 

--- Document Chunk 343 ---
direct utilisation of its resources, both in terms of budget and FTEs.

--- Document Chunk 344 ---
The Agency keeps a strong commitment to deploying the necessary resources to meet 

--- Document Chunk 345 ---
the legal deadlines related to issuing of VA, SSC and ERTMS Trackside approvals, while also 

--- Document Chunk 346 ---
respecting the deadlines for its safety and interoperability related activities, all of which 

--- Document Chunk 347 ---
contribute to the achievement of the high-level policy objectives of the 4th Railway Pack-

--- Document Chunk 348 ---
age. The decision time linked to the authority tasks has undeniably a tremendous impact 

--- Document Chunk 349 ---
on the rail stakeholders and on the competitiveness of rail compared with other sectors. 

--- Document Chunk 350 ---
The Agency therefore strives for an increasingly higher level of efficiency in its authority 

--- Document Chunk 351 ---
tasks, as for its other activities.

--- Document Chunk 352 ---
The Agency has based the 2024 budget envelope on the draft budget proposal of the Eu-

--- Document Chunk 353 ---
ropean Commission and is hopeful that this envelope will be confirmed as the final result 

--- Document Chunk 354 ---
of the EU budget negotiation procedure for 2024. Any cut applied to this envelope would 

--- Document Chunk 355 ---
affect the level of ambition and commitment for the proposed activities in 2024.

--- Document Chunk 356 ---
The Agency would also like to bring forward interesting and new projects  that could 

--- Document Chunk 357 ---
benefit the entire rail sector. Separately to the Single Programming Document, the Agen-

--- Document Chunk 358 ---
cy has put forward a proposal on its resource needs to develop the Information Sharing 

--- Document Chunk 359 ---
System (ISS), which is crucial for the successful implementation of CSM ASLP . The Agency 

--- Document Chunk 360 ---
will continue to work intensely on its NSA monitoring activities, as it is one of the policy 

--- Document Chunk 361 ---
priorities highlighted in the Strengthening Action Plan. In addition, there is a need to de -

--- Document Chunk 362 ---
velop, together with Member States, a new Priority Countries Programme (PCP) at EU level, 

--- Document Chunk 363 ---
with a broader approach which goes beyond the scope of current monitoring activities 

--- Document Chunk 364 ---
of the Agency (e.g. NSA, NoBo, Peer review NIB, etc). The PCP has the potential to provide 

--- Document Chunk 365 ---
a more holistic picture of railway safety and interoperability in the Member States, and 

--- Document Chunk 366 ---
to bring further changes to improve safety across the EU through capacity building and 

--- Document Chunk 367 ---
mutual exchanges. These tasks would need to receive an additional dedicated resource 

--- Document Chunk 368 ---
envelope. The legal framework (current and any potential new evolution) is to be defined.

--- Document Chunk 369 ---
I would like to assure the members of the Management Board that the Agency will con-

--- Document Chunk 370 ---
tinue to implement the mechanism already put in place for a regular monitoring of the 

--- Document Chunk 371 ---
SPD implementation in terms of outputs delivery and resource consumption, as well as 

--- Document Chunk 372 ---
of the Strengthening Action Plan. The Agency will also continue to improve the set of 

--- Document Chunk 373 ---
budget execution monitoring actions already established to make best use of the avail -

--- Document Chunk 374 ---
able budget appropriations. The Agency will strengthen its tools to better plan, monitor, 

--- Document Chunk 375 ---
and report so as to continuously increase its data-driven, transparent working culture. In 

--- Document Chunk 376 ---
addition, more efforts will be produced to achieve more with less resources, as well as en-

--- Document Chunk 377 ---
suring that the processes within the Agency are streamlined to deliver high-quality results 

--- Document Chunk 378 ---
to all our stakeholders, in line with the Strengthening Action Plan 2023-2027.

--- Document Chunk 379 ---
The Agency will also continue to work closely with its stakeholders in order to ensure the 

--- Document Chunk 380 ---
successful implementation of this challenging multi-annual programme. These activities 

--- Document Chunk 381 ---
of the Agency are crucial for contributing to the achievement of a significant modal shift 

--- Document Chunk 382 ---
to rail, in particular by helping to create and manage a Single European Rail Area, and to 

--- Document Chunk 383 ---

--- Document Chunk 384 ---

--- Document Chunk 385 ---

--- Document Chunk 386 ---

--- Document Chunk 387 ---

--- Document Chunk 388 ---

MISSION  STATEMENT | 9

--- Document Chunk 391 ---
Mission statement

--- Document Chunk 392 ---
The vision and mission statements of the Agency (“A sustainable, safe European transport 

--- Document Chunk 393 ---
system without frontiers” and “Moving Europe towards a sustainable and safe railway sys-

--- Document Chunk 394 ---
tem without frontiers” , respectively) were defined in 2021. They reflect its current position 

--- Document Chunk 395 ---
and role, while of course remaining fully in line with the legal mandate of the Agency.

--- Document Chunk 396 ---
The Agency contributes to the further development and effective functioning of a Single 

--- Document Chunk 397 ---
European Railway Area without frontiers, by guaranteeing a high level of railway safety 

--- Document Chunk 398 ---
and interoperability, while improving the competitive position of the railway sector, as 

--- Document Chunk 399 ---
envisaged by the Agency Regulation 2016/796. In particular, the Agency shall contribute, 

--- Document Chunk 400 ---
on technical matters, to the implementation of Union legislation by developing a com -

--- Document Chunk 401 ---
mon approach to safety on the Union rail system and by enhancing the level of interoper-

--- Document Chunk 402 ---
ability on the Union rail system and associated data, with a specific focus on facilitating the 

--- Document Chunk 403 ---
interoperable deployment of ERTMS and on access to data for pushing rail modernisation 

--- Document Chunk 404 ---
and digitalisation. By working in close cooperation with the national authorities acting in 

--- Document Chunk 405 ---
the fields of railway safety and interoperability, the Agency will substantially contribute 

--- Document Chunk 406 ---
to an increased competitiveness of rail and to the seamless cross-border traffic in the EU. 

--- Document Chunk 407 ---
Moreover, through timely delivery of appropriate regulation that reflects the harmonised 

--- Document Chunk 408 ---
and validated solution proposals from the Europe’s Rail Joint Undertaking, the Agency 

--- Document Chunk 409 ---
contributes significantly to the coordinated and rapid deployment of such solutions, thus 

--- Document Chunk 410 ---
strengthening the competitiveness of rail in the transport mix. All these elements are 

--- Document Chunk 411 ---
translated into rail becoming more attractive and affordable for passengers and freight, 

--- Document Chunk 412 ---
with the Agency playing an active role in supporting the delivery of the European Green 

--- Document Chunk 413 ---
Deal for the EU citizens and businesses.

MISSION  STATEMENT | 13

--- Document Chunk 580 ---
I. General context

--- Document Chunk 581 ---
14 | SINGLE PROGRAMMING DOCUMENT 2024-2026

--- Document Chunk 582 ---
General context

--- Document Chunk 583 ---
Transport is an essential part of the European integration, especially given its contribution 

--- Document Chunk 584 ---
to the functioning of the free movement of services, goods, and people. Transport also 

--- Document Chunk 585 ---
represents around 9% of the EU gross added value and directly employs around 11 million 

--- Document Chunk 586 ---
workers (1), therefore representing an important sector for society at large. EU transport 

--- Document Chunk 587 ---
policies have been developed according to the key principles of safety, sustainability, resil-

--- Document Chunk 588 ---
ience, connectivity, and efficiency.

--- Document Chunk 589 ---
Through its long-term vision for the transport sector and European society, the European 

--- Document Chunk 590 ---
Commission published in 2020 the Sustainable and Smart Mobility Strategy with a detailed 

--- Document Chunk 591 ---
action plan of 82 initiatives. With this strategy, the Commission presents how the EU trans-

--- Document Chunk 592 ---
port system will achieve its needed green and digital transformation and become more 

--- Document Chunk 593 ---
resilient. As outlined in the European Green Deal, the result will be a 90% cut in carbon 

--- Document Chunk 594 ---
emissions by 2050. Regarding the rail sector, the following targets have been set:

--- Document Chunk 595 ---
  Traffic on high-speed rail will double by 2030

--- Document Chunk 596 ---
  Rail freight traffic will increase by 50% by 2030 and double by 2050

--- Document Chunk 597 ---
  By 2030, rail and waterborne-based intermodal transport will be able to compete 

--- Document Chunk 598 ---
on equal footing with road-only transport in the EU

--- Document Chunk 599 ---
The European Union Agency for Railways will support the European Commission, in line 

--- Document Chunk 600 ---
with its accountability ceiling, in achieving these goals, in particular through the further 

--- Document Chunk 601 ---
development and effective functioning of a Single European Railway Area without fron -

--- Document Chunk 602 ---
tiers.

--- Document Chunk 603 ---
The 2024-2026 programming period for the Agency involves two different types of activ-

--- Document Chunk 604 ---
ities:

--- Document Chunk 605 ---
  The policy tasks contributing to the implementation of Union legislation by de -

--- Document Chunk 606 ---
veloping a common approach to safety on the Union rail system and by enhanc -

--- Document Chunk 607 ---
ing the level of interoperability on the Union rail system, taking into account the 

--- Document Chunk 608 ---
policy priorities identified in the Strengthening Plan and implemented through 

--- Document Chunk 609 ---
the Strengthening Action Plan 2023-2027.

--- Document Chunk 610 ---
  The fully fledged performance of the Agency’s tasks as EU-wide authority for 

--- Document Chunk 611 ---
safety certification, vehicle authorisation and ERTMS trackside approval, along with 

--- Document Chunk 612 ---
other tasks in the field of railway safety and interoperability as foreseen in the Tech-

--- Document Chunk 613 ---
nical Pillar of the Fourth Railway Package.

--- Document Chunk 614 ---
The Agency continues to implement its work programme following the principles of the 

--- Document Chunk 615 ---
intervention logic, in line with the guidelines provided by the Network of EU Agencies. 

--- Document Chunk 616 ---
The intervention logic supports the Agency by emphasising the desired changes and the 

--- Document Chunk 617 ---
road to its achievement. It is also a thinking process supporting the Agency to design, 

--- Document Chunk 618 ---
reconsider, and adapt its outputs to the most effective one for a determined outcome.

--- Document Chunk 619 ---
The Agency also strives to increase its efficiency in delivering the outcomes and impacts 

--- Document Chunk 620 ---
expected by EU citizens. In light of the above, the work programme of the Agency (in its 

--- Document Chunk 621 ---
multi-annual and annual planning) is organised around seven strategic statements, which 

--- Document Chunk 622 ---
project the Agency’s role in relation to its stakeholders, complemented by two transver -

--- Document Chunk 623 ---
sal strategic statements, which capture the Agency’s governance and support functions. 

--- Document Chunk 624 ---
These strategic statements have been in place since the adoption of SPD 2022-2024 and 

--- Document Chunk 625 ---
are extremely important, as they show the direction of travel on which the Agency plans to 

--- Document Chunk 626 ---
embark in order to make railways work better for society, subject of course to its remit and 

--- Document Chunk 627 ---
accountability ceiling. The concrete Agency work, represented by projects and services 

--- Document Chunk 628 ---
with concrete outputs, is organised by grouping the projects and services which together 

--- Document Chunk 629 ---
can contribute to the outcomes and impacts stated in a particular strategic statement.

--- Document Chunk 630 ---
In addition, SPD 2024-2026 will follow and align itself with the actions and resource allo -

--- Document Chunk 631 ---
cations detailed in the Strengthening Action Plan adopted by the MB in November 2022. 

--- Document Chunk 632 ---
The seven priority areas will be highlighted in the annual section and their importance 

--- Document Chunk 633 ---
(1) https://european-union.europa.eu/priorities-and-actions/actions-topic/transport_en

--- Document Chunk 634 ---

--- Document Chunk 635 ---
will be reflected both in terms of FTE and budget allocation. Of course, the Agency will 

--- Document Chunk 636 ---
remain flexible and redeploy resources if needed but this innovative approach provides 

--- Document Chunk 637 ---
a roadmap for all stakeholders regarding the areas on which the Agency will focus in the 

--- Document Chunk 638 ---
coming years.

--- Document Chunk 639 ---
Thanks to a joint effort with the European Commission and the support from the Man -

--- Document Chunk 640 ---
agement Board, the Agency was granted 12 additional TAs to its establishment plan to 

--- Document Chunk 641 ---
implement the Strengthening Plan. However, these additional resources must be financed 

--- Document Chunk 642 ---
within the existing budget envelope, with no additional subsidy allocation, which creates 

--- Document Chunk 643 ---
a budgetary pressure on the Agency. The Agency proposes in SPD 2024-2026 a robust 

--- Document Chunk 644 ---
budget allocation, which copes with this pressure and provides resources for different 

--- Document Chunk 645 ---
essential activities. However, the budget is based on the assumption that the EC draft 

--- Document Chunk 646 ---
budget proposal will be confirmed at the end of the EU budget negotiation cycle. Any cut 

--- Document Chunk 647 ---
applied to this envelope would jeopardize the basic business continuity for the Agency’s 

--- Document Chunk 648 ---
functions and will affect the level of ambition and commitment for the proposed activities 

--- Document Chunk 649 ---
in 2024.

--- Document Chunk 650 ---
The Agency will pay significant attention to a regular monitoring of the SPD implemen -

--- Document Chunk 651 ---
tation in terms of outputs, resource consumption and revenues, which can allow for agile 

--- Document Chunk 652 ---
responses and possible adaptation of its work programme. The Agency will continue to 

--- Document Chunk 653 ---
work together with the pool of experts for the mutual benefit of the cooperation between 

--- Document Chunk 654 ---
the Agency and the NSAs. This cooperation may also help the Agency to tackle capacity 

--- Document Chunk 655 ---
shortages, as well as language skills gaps. In addition, the Agency will strive for contin -

--- Document Chunk 656 ---
uously improving its efficiency in delivering the expected outputs, as well as its overall 

--- Document Chunk 657 ---
performance in contributing to the expected outcomes and impacts.

--- Document Chunk 737 ---
Content of the multi-annual programme 2024-2026

--- Document Chunk 738 ---
For its 2024-2026 work programme, the Agency considers the possible ways of balancing 

--- Document Chunk 739 ---
the demand for its authority work on one hand and the ambition level for the priority areas 

--- Document Chunk 740 ---
detailed in the Strengthening Plan, on the other hand. The authorisations, certificates and 

--- Document Chunk 741 ---
approvals issued by the Agency have a direct impact on the functioning of the rail sector 

--- Document Chunk 742 ---
and bring much added value in terms of safety and interoperability.

--- Document Chunk 743 ---
Furthermore, subject to additional resources, the Agency intends to implement, together 

--- Document Chunk 744 ---
with Member States, a Priority Country Programme (PCP) which is a strategic initiative that 

--- Document Chunk 745 ---
aims to assess and monitor the state of railway safety and interoperability legislation im -

--- Document Chunk 746 ---
plementation in Member States providing a comprehensive picture of railway safety and 

--- Document Chunk 747 ---
helping the MS to identify areas for improvement. 

--- Document Chunk 748 ---
The focus of this programme will be on the legal set-up and the capability of the organisations 

--- Document Chunk 749 ---
within the Member States to take up the various responsibilities under railway safety and in-

--- Document Chunk 750 ---
teroperability legislation, both at authority as well as operational level. Furthermore, also the 

--- Document Chunk 751 ---
Member State responsibility under EU legislation will be in the scope of the assessments.

--- Document Chunk 752 ---
In this perspective, the Agency has additionally developed a robust business case for the 

--- Document Chunk 753 ---
development of a supporting Information Sharing System (ISS) demonstrating the expected 

--- Document Chunk 754 ---
benefits, clarifying the additional resources needed to develop, deploy, and maintain the ISS 

--- Document Chunk 755 ---
as an IT solution and providing a detailed timetable for implementation spanning from 2024 

--- Document Chunk 756 ---
to 2029. The objective of the ISS initiative is to improve railway safety in the European 

--- Document Chunk 757 ---
Union through the sharing and analysis of relevant safety information, supported 

--- Document Chunk 758 ---
by a pro-active, performing and technology-proof system of data exchange.

--- Document Chunk 759 ---
In addition, the strategic role in policy development, research and innovation, and ad -

--- Document Chunk 760 ---
vice provided by the Agency is recognised as highly important and should continue to 

--- Document Chunk 761 ---
be strengthened. The cooperation with the Europe’s Rail Joint Undertaking is a strategic 

--- Document Chunk 762 ---
long-term activity aimed at ensuring alignment between the EU regulatory framework on 

--- Document Chunk 763 ---
railways and efficient EU funding of rail research. Furthermore, this will continue paving 

--- Document Chunk 764 ---
the way for the inclusion of new technologies in the TSIs and, pending their adoption, in 

--- Document Chunk 765 ---
technical opinions of the Agency. It is equally important to highlight the possible role of 

--- Document Chunk 766 ---
the Agency to monitor and support the adequate implementation of the existing legal 

--- Document Chunk 767 ---
MULTI-ANNUAL PR OGRAMMING  2 024-2 026 | 19

--- Document Chunk 768 ---
framework through a harmonised level of maturity both at the levels of operators and na-

--- Document Chunk 769 ---
tional authorities. To make its operations always more efficient and effective, the Agency 

--- Document Chunk 770 ---
will continue to implement to its full extent the continuous improvement approach to

--- Document Chunk 856 ---
In the field of Railway Interoperability, the Agency has identified so far six intermediate 

--- Document Chunk 857 ---
outcomes that it can actively influence through its portfolio of TSIs, ERTMS, National rules, 

--- Document Chunk 858 ---
and Registers services. They are essential components, which will lead to the achievement 

--- Document Chunk 859 ---
of the strategic statement. The already identified intermediate outcomes are as follows:

--- Document Chunk 860 ---
1. ERTMS is fully implemented on rolling stock by all Railway Undertakings

--- Document Chunk 861 ---
2. ERTMS is fully implemented on railway infrastructure by all Infrastructure Managers

--- Document Chunk 862 ---
3. All railway rolling stock is TSI compliant by all RUs across the EU. (exc. TAP/TAF & OPE)

--- Document Chunk 863 ---
4. All railway infrastructure is TSI compliant by all IMs across the EU

--- Document Chunk 864 ---
5. National rules (rolling stock & fixed installation) are harmonised across the EU

--- Document Chunk 865 ---
6. All relevant railway-related data is shared in an open and transparent way so that it 

--- Document Chunk 866 ---
is utilisable and useful for the sector

--- Document Chunk 867 ---
Of course, this list will continue to evolve in the future to include additional intermediate 

--- Document Chunk 868 ---
outcomes, as the Agency continues to pursue its full implementation of the intervention 

--- Document Chunk 869 ---
logic.

--- Document Chunk 870 ---
Following the results of the MB workshop in June 2022 on SPD 2024-2026, where the Man-

--- Document Chunk 871 ---
agement Board expressed its desire for the Agency to propose more knowledge sharing 

--- Document Chunk 872 ---
activities, such as training, and other dissemination activities, the Agency will strengthen 

--- Document Chunk 873 ---
its activities in this domain. Such activities will be coordinated by the ERA Academy, being 

--- Document Chunk 874 ---
the established knowledge sharing vehicle of the Agency. While being part of Strategic 

--- Document Chunk 875 ---
Statement 7, the ERA Academy activities, by their nature, serve all strategic statements of 

--- Document Chunk 876 ---
the Agency.

--- Document Chunk 877 ---
The Agency will also continue to deliver on its role as sole body responsible for issuing 

--- Document Chunk 878 ---
multi-Member-State authorisations, certifications, and approvals. The Agency will contin-

--- Document Chunk 879 ---
ue performing its tasks in full partnership with the NSAs. In addition, the links between 

--- Document Chunk 880 ---
authorisation, certifications, and approvals by the Agency and the supervision by the NSAs 

--- Document Chunk 881 ---
will be strengthened. The Agency will also continue to drive further the harmonisation 

--- Document Chunk 882 ---
towards the Single European Railway Area, ensuring the path towards technical and oper-

--- Document Chunk 883 ---
ational interoperability. The advancement of the System Pillar and the Agency’s inputs in 

--- Document Chunk 884 ---
the matter will further support harmonisation.

--- Document Chunk 885 ---
The lessons learnt through the issuing of VAs, ERTMS trackside approvals and from the 

--- Document Chunk 886 ---
monitoring of NoBos will be used to capture continuous improvement opportunities for 

--- Document Chunk 887 ---
the technical specifications and to the authorization procedures. The experience in issuing 

--- Document Chunk 888 ---
safety certificates will be used to better steer the safety related policy making, so railway 

--- Document Chunk 889 ---
safety will never be misused again as a barrier. More specifically, the work on NoBo moni-

--- Document Chunk 890 ---
toring will be reinforced in 2024, with additional resources dedicated to this activity, in line 

--- Document Chunk 891 ---
with the direction given in the Strengthening Plan.

--- Document Chunk 892 ---
The stability of the TSIs, together with a successful cleaning up of the remaining national 

--- Document Chunk 893 ---
rules are the foundation of seamless operations across Europe and for an increas -

--- Document Chunk 894 ---
ingly effective authority function, reinforcing the added value of a European mindset in 

--- Document Chunk 895 ---
the EU railway system. In 2024, the Agency will continue to work on the cleaning-up of 

--- Document Chunk 896 ---
national technical and safety rules, as well as those on fixed installation and ERTMS. This 

--- Document Chunk 897 ---
cleaning-up is an important step towards delivering a truly harmonised EU rail system. The 

--- Document Chunk 898 ---
Agency will continue to focus on the removal of redundant national rules (operational 

--- Document Chunk 899 ---
and technical), the harmonisation of the remaining rules and the development of AMOCs.

--- Document Chunk 900 ---
In 2023, the Agency has finalised the cleaning up of the national rules for vehicles. The 

--- Document Chunk 901 ---
Agency has further identified the national rules that should be transferred into the TSIs by 

--- Document Chunk 902 ---
means of further harmonisation, specific cases and closing of open points. This transfer 

--- Document Chunk 903 ---
will take place as of 2024 by means of Change Requests and will result in a significant 

--- Document Chunk 904 ---
reduction of the national rules.

--- Document Chunk 1003 ---
Multi-annual programming 2024-2026

--- Document Chunk 1004 ---
The Agency is playing a pivotal role in supporting the transformation of the European 

--- Document Chunk 1005 ---
transport system towards decarbonised, interoperable, and safe transport modes based 

--- Document Chunk 1006 ---
on multi-modal integration (MaaS).

--- Document Chunk 1007 ---
In 2023, the Agency played a key role for driving the data and digitalisation agenda for 

--- Document Chunk 1008 ---
railways, based on the linked data pilots and the revision of TAP/TAF TSI. Those elements 

--- Document Chunk 1009 ---
are particularly relevant in a multi-modal context as they enable that integration in terms 

--- Document Chunk 1010 ---
of ticketing and timetables which has been preventing the effective development of rail 

--- Document Chunk 1011 ---
as the backbone of a multi-modal and international transport.

--- Document Chunk 1012 ---
The Agency has identified for this Strategic Statement two intermediate outcomes, which 

--- Document Chunk 1013 ---
will support the achievement of the overarching statement. There are the following ones:

--- Document Chunk 1014 ---
1. TAP is implemented by all relevant railway actors (IMs, RUs, ticket vendors), it is actu-

--- Document Chunk 1015 ---
ally used as the main channel of information exchange and the ticketing is integrat-

--- Document Chunk 1016 ---
ed in the multimodal environment with other transport modes

--- Document Chunk 1017 ---
2. TAF is implemented by all relevant railway actors (IMs, RUs, WKs, CTOs) and it is actu-

--- Document Chunk 1018 ---
ally used as the main channel of information exchange

--- Document Chunk 1019 ---
Of course, TAF and TAP TSI will also be in scope for some intermediate outcomes already 

--- Document Chunk 1020 ---
identified under strategic statement 1. Additional intermediate outcomes will be identi -

--- Document Chunk 1021 ---
fied in the future to further implement the intervention logic within the Agency.

--- Document Chunk 1022 ---
For the period 2024-2026, the Agency will still be a top player in ensuring the right frame-

--- Document Chunk 1023 ---
work for the data and information exchange related to assets and services (includ-

--- Document Chunk 1024 ---
ing ticketing data), based on linked data, universal data identifiers and more and better 

--- Document Chunk 1025 ---
data exchanged between operators and customers. This will ensure a seamless exchange 

--- Document Chunk 1026 ---
of data with other modes of transport, thus allowing the customers to benefit from a com-

--- Document Chunk 1027 ---
prehensive logistics chain or the mobility-as-a-service, respectively.

--- Document Chunk 1028 ---
While specifications for infrastructure description related data used in the register of in -

--- Document Chunk 1029 ---
frastructure (RINF), respectively for information exchange in telematics applications, were 

--- Document Chunk 1030 ---
developed for different purposes, they now appear to be inconsistent between one an -

--- Document Chunk 1031 ---
other in the context of their integration into the European Mobility Data Space (EMDS) for 

--- Document Chunk 1032 ---
which the ERA Vocabulary has been set as building block for rail. Corresponding alignment 

--- Document Chunk 1033 ---
and linking of rail data for infrastructure description constitutes both an internal and ex -

--- Document Chunk 1034 ---
ternal challenge for the Agency that will be addressed through the work of the Agency 

--- Document Chunk 1035 ---
on the review of the governance of location coding in the context of the review of TSIs 

--- Document Chunk 1036 ---
on telematics applications and development of the RINF Regulation and associated RINF 

--- Document Chunk 1037 ---
application.

--- Document Chunk 1038 ---
Moreover, the Agency is a publisher in the open data portal, with 13 datasets published. 

--- Document Chunk 1039 ---
Currently, the Agency is developing the strategic direction for linked data under strategic 

--- Document Chunk 1040 ---
statement 8, while exploring the mainstreaming of this approach to other registers and 

--- Document Chunk 1041 ---
databases. Once moved from a strategic development concept to a mainstreamed ap -

--- Document Chunk 1042 ---
proach, this stream of work will be covered under strategic statement 2 and 3. In addition, 

--- Document Chunk 1043 ---
the TAF TSI will provide the data communication requirements for the transparent and 

--- Document Chunk 1044 ---
efficient traffic management and train operations system of the future including also (i) 

--- Document Chunk 1045 ---
first and last mile logistic segments involving intermodal actors (operators, terminals) and 

--- Document Chunk 1046 ---
(ii) linkage to other modes of transport (road, waterborne). This will also contain the en -

--- Document Chunk 1047 ---
hanced simple and smart tracking of trains, wagons and consignments. The same TSI will 

--- Document Chunk 1048 ---
also include additional requirements for the setting up of LaaS starting from consignment 

--- Document Chunk 1049 ---
order (intermodal compliant), train operation preparation and ending in well-predicted / 

--- Document Chunk 1050 ---
efficient delivery of trains, wagons and consignments to the business partners.

--- Document Chunk 1051 ---
Concerning the environmental sustainability of the railway system, the Agency will contin-

--- Document Chunk 1052 ---
ue to deliver support and assistance to the EC on rail and sustainability with annual topical 

--- Document Chunk 1053 ---
reports, as well as for the coordination of transport of dangerous goods by rail, 

--- Document Chunk 1054 ---
recognising of course the supporting essence of the Agency’s role in the matter.

--- Document Chunk 1055 ---
Strategic Statement 2 & 3

that supports an environmentally

In the field of Railway Safety, the Agency has identified 3 categories of intermediate out -

--- Document Chunk 1081 ---
comes that it can actively influence through its portfolio of safety related projects and 

--- Document Chunk 1082 ---
services and that are essential pre-conditions to achieve the strategic statement 4. The 

--- Document Chunk 1083 ---
identified intermediate outcomes are as follows:

--- Document Chunk 1084 ---
1. All railway operators – IM, RU, ECM - understand and accept their responsibility and 

--- Document Chunk 1085 ---
actively implement an SMS to control the risks of operational activities;

--- Document Chunk 1086 ---
2. An increased performance of and trust in the different safety related control levels in 

--- Document Chunk 1087 ---
the system - ERA, MS, NSA, ASBO, ECM CB, accreditation, recognition, NIB;

--- Document Chunk 1088 ---
3. Safety and safety management/performance related data is shared in an open and 

--- Document Chunk 1089 ---
transparent way;

--- Document Chunk 1090 ---
Up until now the Agency has invested most of its efforts in building knowledge and reg -

--- Document Chunk 1091 ---
ulating, while not sufficiently supporting the railway sector in the actual implementation 

--- Document Chunk 1092 ---
of the legislative framework. The following years of the Agency’s work programme will 

--- Document Chunk 1093 ---
focus more on the actual implementation by supporting the sector through knowledge 

--- Document Chunk 1094 ---
sharing, by better understanding the issues the sector is facing when implementing the 

--- Document Chunk 1095 ---
legislative framework, by reinforcing the expected outcome where possible and enforcing 

--- Document Chunk 1096 ---
it where necessary. Within this framework of intermediate outcomes and interventions for 

--- Document Chunk 1097 ---
statement 4 the Agency will continue to focus on:

--- Document Chunk 1098 ---
1. Supporting Member States in developing, adopting and repealing national legis-

--- Document Chunk 1099 ---
lation and strengthening NSAs’ and NIBs’ capacity, in line with principles and legal 

--- Document Chunk 1100 ---
acts promoted by the EU. (sharing knowledge/ monitoring/ reinforcing)

--- Document Chunk 1101 ---
2. Enhancing railway safety through positive safety culture and integration of 

--- Document Chunk 1102 ---
human and organisational factors  and on the harmonisation of the safety 

--- Document Chunk 1103 ---
approach, partly through SSC applications. (sharing knowledge/ monitoring/ 

--- Document Chunk 1104 ---
reinforcing)

--- Document Chunk 1105 ---
3. Monitoring of NSAs and the follow-up of issues emerged during the 1

--- Document Chunk 1106 ---
st cycle of 

--- Document Chunk 1107 ---
audits (monitoring / reinforcing). By the end of the 2nd cycle, reflection as to wheth-

--- Document Chunk 1108 ---
er changes to the current framework are needed will be made and appropriate pro-

--- Document Chunk 1162 ---

--- Document Chunk 1163 ---

--- Document Chunk 1164 ---
the entrance of new operators in the market.

--- Document Chunk 1165 ---

--- Document Chunk 1166 ---
nomic impact of the vehicle authorisation and issuing of single safety certificate 

--- Document Chunk 1167 ---
processes on the railway sector, the impact of the TSIs as a package, of market open-

--- Document Chunk 1168 ---
ing and competition and of modular interchangeability in the ERTMS system spec-

--- Document Chunk 1169 ---
ifications. The Agency will assess interoperability and safety improvements from a 

--- Document Chunk 1170 ---
cost-effectiveness perspective, also considering efficiency and effectiveness of the 

--- Document Chunk 1171 ---
Agency’s internal processes. The results of the assessments will be used to propose rec -

--- Document Chunk 1172 ---
ommendations for improving the legal texts, as well as any non-regulatory instruments, 

--- Document Chunk 1173 ---
in the spirit of the Better Regulation principles. Building on the IA work in the past years, 

--- Document Chunk 1174 ---

--- Document Chunk 1175 ---
holder feedback on the IAs. In addition, the Management Board, NSA and NRB networks 

--- Document Chunk 1176 ---

--- Document Chunk 1177 ---
the IA practice. Furthermore, the important work on women in transport, which should 

--- Document Chunk 1178 ---
lead to the strengthening of women’s employment and equal opportunities for women 

--- Document Chunk 1179 ---
and men in the transport sector will be pursued. Indeed, many studies have shown that 

--- Document Chunk 1180 ---
gender parity in the workforce increases the productivity and the cohesion of staff. In addi-

--- Document Chunk 1181 ---

--- Document Chunk 1203 ---

--- Document Chunk 1204 ---

--- Document Chunk 1206 ---

--- Document Chunk 1207 ---

--- Document Chunk 1208 ---

MULTI-ANNUAL PR OGRAMMING  2 024-2 026 | 37

--- Document Chunk 1485 ---
Strategy for achieving efficiency gains

--- Document Chunk 1486 ---
The Agency is committed to continuously improving its functioning, streamlining its pro-

--- Document Chunk 1487 ---
cesses, optimising the engagement of its staff, and allowing for the reallocation of re -

--- Document Chunk 1488 ---
sources to the most important priorities. In the course of 2021, the Agency worked quite 

--- Document Chunk 1489 ---
intensively on efficiency gains. This work progressed until the end of 2021 and led to the 

--- Document Chunk 1490 ---
drafting of the Strengthening Plan, finalised, and endorsed by the Management Board at 

--- Document Chunk 1491 ---
the beginning of 2022. The purpose of the Strengthening Plan is to make the strongest 

--- Document Chunk 1492 ---
possible case in order to strengthen the Agency with resources matching the level of 

--- Document Chunk 1493 ---
ambition necessary for achieving the important EC policy objectives for rail, in an effective 

--- Document Chunk 1494 ---
and efficient manner, and benefit from high levels of ambition and efficiency within ERA’s 

--- Document Chunk 1495 ---
structure and methods.

--- Document Chunk 1496 ---
With the document serving as a basis for the internal EC budget negotiations in 2022, the 

--- Document Chunk 1497 ---
Agency received a proposed increase of 12 TAs in 2022. While the additional TA allocation 

--- Document Chunk 1498 ---
is lower compared to the request from the Strengthening Plan (12 TAs proposed out of the 

--- Document Chunk 1499 ---
22 TAs requested), it can offer a good basis for the Agency to proceed with the implemen-

--- Document Chunk 1500 ---
tation of the Strengthening Plan.

--- Document Chunk 1501 ---
Following the adoption of the aforementioned plan, the Agency prepared the Strength -

--- Document Chunk 1502 ---
ening Action Plan (SAP) 2023-2027, which details the actions that will be carried out within 

--- Document Chunk 1503 ---
the next five years to strengthen the Agency’s efficiency. The SAP 2023-2027 is organised 

--- Document Chunk 1504 ---
along the following components/objectives:

--- Document Chunk 1505 ---
a.)  Drive an optimal resourcing of the following policy priority areas, matched by pro-

--- Document Chunk 1506 ---
portional outputs and outcomes, including efficiency gains:

--- Document Chunk 1507 ---
  NSA and Nobo monitoring

--- Document Chunk 1508 ---
  ERTMS and radio communication evolution

--- Document Chunk 1509 ---
  TSI related work

--- Document Chunk 1510 ---
  Clean-up of national rules

--- Document Chunk 1511 ---
  CSM ASLP

--- Document Chunk 1512 ---
  Digitalisation of the Agency’s registers

--- Document Chunk 1513 ---
b.)  Maintain proper resourcing and further efficiency gains for the authority tasks,

--- Document Chunk 1514 ---
c.)  Ensure a reduction in the Agency’s administrative FTE allocation while maintaining 

--- Document Chunk 1515 ---
regularity and legality. This will be possible thanks no but not limited to:

--- Document Chunk 1516 ---
  A workload analysis

--- Document Chunk 1517 ---
  The Leaning of processes

--- Document Chunk 1518 ---
  A training programme to facilitate the transition and provide the required 

--- Document Chunk 1519 ---
technical skills to staff moving from administrative tasks to operational ones

--- Document Chunk 1520 ---
d.)  Ensure the overall projected FTE evolution by 2027

--- Document Chunk 1521 ---
e.)  Ensure effective and efficient budget management (planning and execution), ap -

--- Document Chunk 1522 ---
propriate risk management

--- Document Chunk 1523 ---
In order to ensure active involvement from all units across the agency and to monitor 

--- Document Chunk 1524 ---
the implementation of the SAP , an internal task force has been set up in 2023. This task 

--- Document Chunk 1525 ---
force ensures optimal communication across the Agency on the SAP and its milestones, 

--- Document Chunk 1526 ---
as well as the implementation of key milestones. Finally, the Strengthening Action Plan has 

--- Document Chunk 1527 ---
been added to the Strategic Calendar of the Executive Board of the Agency. A rapporteur 

--- Document Chunk 1528 ---
has been appointed in 2023, who will support, guide, and monitor the implementation 

--- Document Chunk 1529 ---
throughout 2024-2026.

--- Document Chunk 1530 ---
38 | SINGLE PROGRAMMING DOCUMENT 2024-2026

--- Document Chunk 1531 ---
Multi-annual programming 2024-2026

--- Document Chunk 1532 ---
Negative priorities / decrease of existing tasks

--- Document Chunk 1533 ---
Paused activities for the year 2024

--- Document Chunk 1534 ---
  NSA Annual Performance review

--- Document Chunk 1535 ---
  Review of NIB accident investigation reports

--- Document Chunk 1536 ---
Stretched and targeted outputs for the year 2024

--- Document Chunk 1537 ---
  The Agency has been working on the Common Safety Methods on the assessment 

--- Document Chunk 1538 ---
of Safety Level and Safety Performance for several years, following its mandate. It 

--- Document Chunk 1539 ---
also is one of the priorities of the Strengthening Action Plan. However, an informa-

--- Document Chunk 1540 ---
tion sharing system is needed to prevent future accidents and improve safety as 

--- Document Chunk 1541 ---
a whole. The Agency does not have sufficient resources to create such tool. The 

--- Document Chunk 1542 ---
Agency has therefore developed a paper with the resources required to develop 

--- Document Chunk 1543 ---
and implement such tool, along with a timeline and the stages of implementation. 

--- Document Chunk 1544 ---
The Information Sharing System (ISS) would require an estimated 2,375,000 EUR 

--- Document Chunk 1545 ---
budget and a total of 8 FTEs. Based on substantial efforts, given the already very 

--- Document Chunk 1546 ---
stretched budget envelope, the Agency allocated 185,000 EUR from its budget in 

--- Document Chunk 1547 ---
2024 to carry out the preliminary work for ISS-Stage 1. This investment needs to 

--- Document Chunk 1548 ---
be complemented with the requested FTEs and budget (as per the dedicated SOS 

--- Document Chunk 1549 ---
paper submitted to the MB), in order to ensure the project materialises its outputs 

--- Document Chunk 1550 ---
and impacts.

--- Document Chunk 1551 ---
  The Agency will continue to work intensely on its NSA monitoring activities, as it is 

--- Document Chunk 1552 ---
one of the policy priorities highlighted in the Strengthening Action Plan. However, 

--- Document Chunk 1553 ---
there is a need to develop together with Member States a new Priority Countries 

--- Document Chunk 1554 ---
Programme (PCP) at EU level, with a broader approach including more railway 

--- Document Chunk 1555 ---
stakeholders such as Member States, NSA/NIB, RUs, IMs, AsBo, NoBo, Notifying 

--- Document Chunk 1556 ---
Authorities, National Accreditation Bodies and other checking bodies, and finally 

--- Document Chunk 1557 ---
other operational stakeholders such as ECM, and wagon keepers. The PCP has the 

--- Document Chunk 1558 ---
potential to provide a more holistic picture of railway safety and interoperability in 

--- Document Chunk 1559 ---
the Member State, and to bring further changes to improve safety across the EU. 

--- Document Chunk 1560 ---
In order to deliver this new initiative, the Agency would need an additional 50,000 

--- Document Chunk 1561 ---
EUR per year, along with 3 FTEs.

--- Document Chunk 1562 ---

--- Document Chunk 1566 ---
Annual Work programme 2024

--- Document Chunk 1567 ---
Executive summary

--- Document Chunk 1568 ---
The Annual Work Programme for 2024 details all the projects and services which will be 

--- Document Chunk 1569 ---
carried out to contribute to the Agency’s goals in the year. The structure of the Work Pro -

--- Document Chunk 1570 ---
gramme has been organised against desired long-term outcomes, implementing there -

--- Document Chunk 1571 ---
fore an effective multi-annual work programme with developed objectives, as well as the 

--- Document Chunk 1572 ---
intervention logic.

--- Document Chunk 1573 ---
The annual work programme 2024 had been aligned to the priorities listed in the Agency’s 

--- Document Chunk 1574 ---
Strengthening Plan and the corresponding implementing document (SAP 2023-2027), 

--- Document Chunk 1575 ---
which represents an anchor for the planning in SPD 2024 and the subsequent ones.

--- Document Chunk 1576 ---
The Agency’s efforts in 2024 are particularly focused on:

--- Document Chunk 1577 ---
  Technical and operational barriers: The Agency will work towards the reduc-

--- Document Chunk 1578 ---
tion of technical and operations barriers within the rail market through, among 

--- Document Chunk 1579 ---
others, the amendment of TSIs to be aligned with the technical innovations, har -

--- Document Chunk 1580 ---
monisation of national rules among MSs, continuous NoBo monitoring, the deliv -

--- Document Chunk 1581 ---
ery of 4

--- Document Chunk 1582 ---
th Railway package activities (SSC, ERTMS TA, VA), and the deployment of 

--- Document Chunk 1583 ---
ERTMS.

--- Document Chunk 1584 ---
  Safety: The Agency will strengthen safety on rail through the development of 

--- Document Chunk 1585 ---
a safety culture, the monitoring of National Safety Authority, the Common Safe -

--- Document Chunk 1586 ---
ty Methods on Assessment of Safety Level and Safety Performance (within the 

--- Document Chunk 1587 ---
boundaries linked to the resource constraints for the information sharing system), 

--- Document Chunk 1588 ---
and other relevant projects.

--- Document Chunk 1589 ---
  Data developments and ticketing: The Agency will continue to foster develop-

--- Document Chunk 1590 ---
ments in the field of Linked data, as well as development under the TAP TSI. The 

--- Document Chunk 1591 ---
Agency will continue its work on databases and registers optimisation.

--- Document Chunk 1592 ---
  Communication and dissemination: The Agency will increase communicating 

--- Document Chunk 1593 ---
and disseminating relevant information and knowledge to its stakeholders, as well 

--- Document Chunk 1594 ---
as organising events and showcase the interesting projects and developments 

--- Document Chunk 1595 ---
within the rail sector.

--- Document Chunk 1596 ---
  Good governance: The Agency will strive for governance excellence and effi -

--- Document Chunk 1597 ---
ciency in all of its activities and will continue its efforts for improving budget exe -

--- Document Chunk 1598 ---
cution rates and overall compliance and performance.

--- Document Chunk 1599 ---

--- Document Chunk 1601 ---
in the annual tables hereinbelow. Moreover, the number of FTEs linked to SAP 2023-2027

is also highlighted in a separate column.

The expected outcomes are further detailed to the following intermediate outcomes more directly linked to the Agency’s safety portfolio:

--- Document Chunk 1612 ---
1. ERTMS is fully implemented on rolling stock by all Railway Undertakings

--- Document Chunk 1613 ---
2. ERTMS is fully implemented on railway infrastructure by all Infrastructure Managers

--- Document Chunk 1614 ---
3. All railway rolling stock is TSI compliant by all Rus across the EU. (exc. TAP/TAF & OPE)

--- Document Chunk 1615 ---
4. All railway infrastructure is TSI compliant by all Ims across the EU

--- Document Chunk 1616 ---
5. National rules (rolling stock & fixed installation) are harmonised across the EU

--- Document Chunk 1617 ---
6. All relevant railway-related data is shared in an open and transparent way so that it is utilisable and useful for the sector

--- Document Chunk 3231 ---
The following general principles guide the application of the legal framework concerning 

--- Document Chunk 3232 ---
the Agency staff:

--- Document Chunk 3233 ---
a.)  The core of the Agency staff consists of Temporary Agents. All Temporary Agent 

--- Document Chunk 3234 ---
positions have been identified as long-term positions. Due to the budgetary and 

--- Document Chunk 3235 ---
establishment plan constraints the Agency is obliged to also engage Contract 

--- Document Chunk 3236 ---
Agents in order to fulfil its mission;

--- Document Chunk 3237 ---
b.)  Temporary and Contract Agents are treated equivalently as far as possible.

--- Document Chunk 3238 ---
In addition, it should be noted the Agency does not employ officials. However, there are 

--- Document Chunk 3239 ---
cases where EU officials have been engaged following an external selection procedure 

--- Document Chunk 3240 ---
and have therefore acquired the status of Temporary Agent in the Agency (whilst remain-

--- Document Chunk 3241 ---
ing an official on unpaid leave in their institution of origin).

--- Document Chunk 3242 ---
Selection and engagement procedures:

--- Document Chunk 3243 ---
The procedure for selection and engagement of Temporary Agents and Contract Agents 

--- Document Chunk 3244 ---
is based on Articles 27-34 of the Staff Regulations and Articles 12-15 and 82-84 of the 

--- Document Chunk 3245 ---
Conditions of Employment of Other Servants of the European Communities (CEOS ), the 

--- Document Chunk 3246 ---
related Implementing Rules on the engagement and use of Temporary Agents and Con -

--- Document Chunk 3247 ---
tract Agents, the Financial Regulation (European Commission’s Framework and that of the 

--- Document Chunk 3248 ---
Agency), the Code of Good Administrative Behaviour and the data protection rules.

--- Document Chunk 3249 ---
The Agency also makes use of the EPSO CAST lists accessible to Agencies for the engage-

--- Document Chunk 3250 ---
ment of Contract Agents. Because of the Agreement on the European Economic Area 

--- Document Chunk 3251 ---
nationals of Norway, Iceland and Liechtenstein are eligible for working for the Agency.

--- Document Chunk 3252 ---
(53) MB	Decision	n°204	 on 	 middle 	 management 	 staff

--- Document Chunk 3253 ---
(54) MB	Decision	n°203	 on 	 types 	 of 	 post 	 and 	 post 	 titles 	 in 	 ERA

--- Document Chunk 3254 ---
(55) MB	Decision	n°326	 on 	 types 	 of 	 posts 	 and	 post	titles

--- Document Chunk 3255 ---
HUMAN R ESOURCES  2024-2026 – QUALITATIVE | 83

--- Document Chunk 3256 ---
The selection procedures for the engagement of Temporary Agents are carried out in ac -

--- Document Chunk 3257 ---
cordance with Decision N° 121 of the Administrative Board of the European Railway Agen-

--- Document Chunk 3258 ---
cy laying down the general implementing provisions on the procedure governing the 

--- Document Chunk 3259 ---
engagement and use of temporary staff under Article 2(f ) of the CEOS.

--- Document Chunk 3260 ---
Depending on the function and the level of tasks and within the limits authorised by the 

--- Document Chunk 3261 ---
establishment plan of the Agency, Temporary Agents are engaged at the following entry 

--- Document Chunk 3262 ---
grades:

--- Document Chunk 3263 ---
  AST 1 to AST 4 for the function group AST

--- Document Chunk 3264 ---
  AD 5 to AD8 for the function group AD

--- Document Chunk 3265 ---
For managerial posts or highly specialised posts, the Agency can engage Temporary 

--- Document Chunk 3266 ---
Agents at grades AD 9 and AD10 or at grade AD12 for Heads of Department.

--- Document Chunk 3267 ---
The duration of contracts for Temporary Agents is governed by Decision N° ERA-ED-

--- Document Chunk 3268 ---
DEC-1109-2015. Staff holding a long-term post are normally offered an initial contract with 

--- Document Chunk 3269 ---
a duration of four years with the possibility of renewal. The standard practice for a first re-

--- Document Chunk 3270 ---
newal is normally for a two-year period and any further renewal is for an indefinite period.

--- Document Chunk 3271 ---
For staff on short-term employment, the duration of the contract depends on the dura -

--- Document Chunk 3272 ---
tion of the tasks to be carried out. At ERA, the duration of those contracts is predominantly 

--- Document Chunk 3273 ---
related to the availability and duration of grants, or to a specific time determined project. 

--- Document Chunk 3274 ---
In very rare cases it is to cover long-term absences.

--- Document Chunk 3275 ---
The Agency is launching the following types of calls, published on ERA website’s Recruit-

--- Document Chunk 3276 ---
ment portal:

--- Document Chunk 3277 ---
  Call for Interest (partial internal re-assignment): CFI/ERA/…

--- Document Chunk 3278 ---
  Internal Mobility for Temporary Agents-Administrators: IM/ERA/AD/…

--- Document Chunk 3279 ---
  Internal Mobility for Temporary Agents-Assistants: IM/ERA/AST/…

--- Document Chunk 3280 ---
  Inter-Agency Mobility for Temporary Agents-Administrators: IAM/ERA/AD/…

--- Document Chunk 3281 ---
  Inter-Agency Mobility for Temporary Agents-Assistants: IAM/ERA/AST/…

--- Document Chunk 3282 ---
  External calls for Temporary Agents-Administrators: ERA/AD/2021/…

--- Document Chunk 3283 ---
  External calls for Temporary Agents-Assistants: ERA/AST/…

--- Document Chunk 3284 ---
  External calls for Contract Agents: ERA/CA/2021/…

--- Document Chunk 3285 ---
Temporary agents

--- Document Chunk 3286 ---
The ERA Regulation 2016/796 which entered into force in 2016 makes no distinction be -

--- Document Chunk 3287 ---
tween posts for long- term and short-term employment. Still a post can, in accordance 

--- Document Chunk 3288 ---
with Article 16 of Decision N° 121, be defined to be for short-term employment when it 

--- Document Chunk 3289 ---
involves tasks of a limited duration.

--- Document Chunk 3290 ---
The decision to renew contracts of employment of Temporary Agents occupying a long-

--- Document Chunk 3291 ---
term post is taken by the Executive Director based on two considerations: the continuity 

--- Document Chunk 3292 ---
of the post and the competences and performances of the jobholder, in accordance with 

--- Document Chunk 3293 ---
Decision N° ERA-ED-DEC-678-2013 and the Procedure PRO_STA_01 on the “renewal and 

--- Document Chunk 3294 ---
non-renewal of contracts of employment before the expiry date” .

--- Document Chunk 3295 ---
If a TA or former TA is awarded a second contract of employment in the same function 

--- Document Chunk 3296 ---
group, this contract shall be considered as a renewal in the sense of Article 8 of the CEOS if 

--- Document Chunk 3297 ---
the period between the end of the first contract and the starting date of the new contract 

--- Document Chunk 3298 ---
is less than 6 months. If the period between the two contracts of employment is 6 months 

--- Document Chunk 3299 ---
or more or if the new contract is in a different function group, the second contract of em-

--- Document Chunk 3300 ---
ployment shall be considered a new contract of employment.

--- Document Chunk 3301 ---
84 | SINGLE PROGRAMMING DOCUMENT 2024-2026

--- Document Chunk 3302 ---
Annexes

--- Document Chunk 3303 ---
Contract agents

--- Document Chunk 3304 ---
The selection procedures for the engagement of Contract Agents are carried out in ac -

--- Document Chunk 3305 ---
cordance with Decision n° 210 of the Management Board of the European Union Agency 

--- Document Chunk 3306 ---
on the general provisions for implementing Article 79(2) of the CEOS, governing the con-

--- Document Chunk 3307 ---
ditions of employment of contract staff employed under the terms of Article 3a thereof.

--- Document Chunk 3308 ---
In accordance with Article 85 of the CEOS, contract staff can be engaged for a fixed pe -

--- Document Chunk 3309 ---
riod of at least three months and not more than five years. Contract Agents are engaged 

--- Document Chunk 3310 ---
for their specific competence in different areas of administration (finance, HR, IT, logistics, 

--- Document Chunk 3311 ---
legal, audit, quality management), in the railway domain or to perform manual or admin -

--- Document Chunk 3312 ---
istrative tasks.

--- Document Chunk 3313 ---
This type of contract is usually used to meet specific needs such as:

--- Document Chunk 3314 ---
  Administrative tasks;

--- Document Chunk 3315 ---
  Coping with temporary peaks in workloads;

--- Document Chunk 3316 ---
  Launching projects or new activities for which long-term commitment in 

--- Document Chunk 3317 ---
terms of staffing is unclear;

--- Document Chunk 3318 ---
  Replacing staff on long-term absences such as maternity leave, long-term sick 

--- Document Chunk 3319 ---
leave or unpaid leave;

--- Document Chunk 3320 ---
However, increasingly ERA has also engaged Contract Agents for other (long-term) tasks, 

--- Document Chunk 3321 ---
such as:

--- Document Chunk 3322 ---
  Administrative and Logistician Support Agents

--- Document Chunk 3323 ---
  Assistants

--- Document Chunk 3324 ---
  Project Officers

--- Document Chunk 3325 ---
Seconded National Experts (56)

--- Document Chunk 3326 ---
Seconded National Experts (SNEs) are staff employed by a national, regional or local pub-

--- Document Chunk 3327 ---
lic administration or a public intergovernmental organisation who are seconded to the 

--- Document Chunk 3328 ---
Agency so that it can use their expertise in a particular field. SNEs are seconded from 

--- Document Chunk 3329 ---
their national employer to the Agency’s operational units on the basis of their specific 

--- Document Chunk 3330 ---
competency and technical expertise in the railway domain, based on Decision n° 173 of 

--- Document Chunk 3331 ---
the Management Board of the European Union Agency for Railways laying down rules 

--- Document Chunk 3332 ---
on the secondment to the Agency of seconded national experts and national experts in 

--- Document Chunk 3333 ---
professional training.

--- Document Chunk 3334 ---
A possibility to mandate ‘cost-free’ SNEs also exists, where the Agency does not pay any 

--- Document Chunk 3335 ---
allowances or cover any of the expenses related to the performance of their duties during 

--- Document Chunk 3336 ---
their secondment, although the Agency does not deploy such SNEs at the moment.

--- Document Chunk 3337 ---
SNEs assist the Agency staff and cannot perform (middle) management duties. The initial 

--- Document Chunk 3338 ---
period of secondment may not be less than six months or more than two years. It may be 

--- Document Chunk 3339 ---
renewed once or more up to a total period not exceeding four years. Exceptionally, the 

--- Document Chunk 3340 ---
Agency’s Executive Director may authorise one more extension of the secondment for 

--- Document Chunk 3341 ---
the maximum duration of one year at the end of the four-year period. Each secondment 

--- Document Chunk 3342 ---
and extension are subject to an exchange of letters. An SNE may be seconded once again 

--- Document Chunk 3343 ---
provided that the conditions of secondment still exist and a period of at least six years has 

--- Document Chunk 3344 ---
elapsed between the end of the previous secondment and the new secondment unless 

--- Document Chunk 3345 ---
the previous secondments lasted for less than four years.

--- Document Chunk 3346 ---
(56)	 SNEs	are	not	employed	by	the	Agency

--- Document Chunk 3347 ---

--- Document Chunk 3468 ---
Mobility policy

--- Document Chunk 3469 ---
Mobility within the Agency

--- Document Chunk 3470 ---
Decision N° 121 of the Administrative Board of the European Railway Agency laying down 

--- Document Chunk 3471 ---
the general implementing provisions on the procedure governing the engagement and 

--- Document Chunk 3472 ---
use of temporary staff under Article 2(f ) of the CEOS (adopted on 25.11.2016) and De -

--- Document Chunk 3473 ---
cision n° 210 of the Management Board of the European Union Agency on the general 

--- Document Chunk 3474 ---
provisions for implementing Article 79(2) of the CEOS, governing the conditions of em -

--- Document Chunk 3475 ---
ployment of contract staff employed under the terms of Article 3a thereof enshrine the 

--- Document Chunk 3476 ---
scenarios for internal mobility for TA 2(f ) and CA.

--- Document Chunk 3477 ---
The Agency considers internal mobility when vacancies arise, but due to the very specific, 

--- Document Chunk 3478 ---
technical competences of a big part of the staff, internal mobility remains limited.

--- Document Chunk 3479 ---
Furthermore, members of the Agency staff can apply for vacant posts within the Agency 

--- Document Chunk 3480 ---
advertised externally. A supplementary agreement in accordance with Article 10 of the 

--- Document Chunk 3481 ---
CEOS will be concluded as required if existing staff get a new job.

--- Document Chunk 3482 ---
Mobility between Union Agencies

--- Document Chunk 3483 ---
The implementing rules on the engagement and use of Temporary Agents 2(f ) and Con-

--- Document Chunk 3484 ---
tract Agents define the scope of mobility between EU Agencies. A very limited number 

--- Document Chunk 3485 ---
of the support staff who have left the Agency in previous years have accepted TA/CA 

--- Document Chunk 3486 ---
positions in other Agencies.

--- Document Chunk 3487 ---
Increasingly staff members who took up long-term Temporary Agent positions at the 

--- Document Chunk 3488 ---
Agency come from other EU Agencies.

--- Document Chunk 3489 ---
Mobility between the agencies and the institutions

--- Document Chunk 3490 ---
Some posts are filled following an external selection procedure by staff coming from other 

--- Document Chunk 3491 ---
European institutions (in particular the Commission), although the number remains small.

ENVIRONMENT  MANAGEMENT  | 93

--- Document Chunk 3610 ---
Annex VI. Environment 

--- Document Chunk 3611 ---
management

--- Document Chunk 3612 ---
Executive summary

--- Document Chunk 3613 ---
The revised SPD guidelines  (63) require Agencies to compile and formalise their Environ-

--- Document Chunk 3614 ---
ment management policy. To achieve this ambition, the first Environment management 

--- Document Chunk 3615 ---
annex was drafted in which ERA summarised its commitment to higher policy goals, 

--- Document Chunk 3616 ---
the measures already in place, as well as the potential future environment man -

--- Document Chunk 3617 ---
agement initiatives and actions , taking in consideration the responsibilities of the 

--- Document Chunk 3618 ---
Agency as a public administration body, while keeping in mind the impact of environ -

--- Document Chunk 3619 ---
mental initiatives on the Agency’s limited human and financial resources. Despite these 

--- Document Chunk 3620 ---
limitations, the Agency is a socially and environmentally responsible organisation which 

--- Document Chunk 3621 ---
pursues, whenever possible, the adoption and related implementation of environmental 

--- Document Chunk 3622 ---
measures and initiatives that can be achieved with the available means.

--- Document Chunk 3623 ---
The Agency is committed to promote a culture of sustainability acting in a re -

--- Document Chunk 3624 ---
sponsible and sustainable manner  – see point 9 of the European Union Agency for 

--- Document Chunk 3625 ---
Railways Policy

--- Document Chunk 3626 ---
 (64). Concern for the environment and promoting a broader sustainability 

--- Document Chunk 3627 ---
agenda are integral to ERA’s professional activities and the management of the organisa-

--- Document Chunk 3628 ---
tion. In addition, the Agency is committed to urgently respond, within the boundaries 

--- Document Chunk 3629 ---
of its mandate and capacity, to the ongoing energy crisis.

--- Document Chunk 3630 ---
The Agency’s aim is to follow and to promote good sustainability practice, to reduce the 

--- Document Chunk 3631 ---
environmental impacts of its activities and to help its stakeholders to do the same. The 

--- Document Chunk 3632 ---

--- Document Chunk 3633 ---

nual Work Programme, in particular Strategic Statement 2 (67) and the specific project des-

ignated to “Green agenda” (ERA1234).

--- Document Chunk 3659 ---
house gas emissions by at least 55% by 2030, compared to 1990 levels – as defined in the 

--- Document Chunk 3660 ---
EU Climate Target Plan 2030 (69).

--- Document Chunk 3661 ---
Since the publication of the Communication from the Commission on the European 

--- Document Chunk 3662 ---
Green Deal (70) in December 2019, ERA has strengthened its activities aiming at promoting 

--- Document Chunk 3663 ---
the role of the railways in the decarbonation of the European transport sector. To make the 

--- Document Chunk 3664 ---
European Union the first carbon neutral region in the world by 2050, lowering the trans -

--- Document Chunk 3665 ---
port emissions is crucial. Between 1990 and 2019, the transport emissions have gradually 

--- Document Chunk 3666 ---
increased and reached 25% of the total greenhouse gas emissions of the EU. The transport 

--- Document Chunk 3667 ---
sector is the second sector only to the energy sector in terms of emission.

--- Document Chunk 3668 ---
However, looking at the same period, the emissions of the railway sector have gradually 

--- Document Chunk 3669 ---
decreased and nowadays represent less than 0.5% of the transport-related emissions. In 

--- Document Chunk 3670 ---
addition, railways are also the mode of transport with the lowest external costs (external -

--- Document Chunk 3671 ---
ities).

--- Document Chunk 3672 ---
ERA has a central role in fostering interoperability and safety of the rail transport which 

--- Document Chunk 3673 ---
should eventually make it more attractive, more efficient and thereby increase the modal 

--- Document Chunk 3674 ---
share of the railways, resulting the greenhouse gas emissions of Europe’s transport sector, 

--- Document Chunk 3675 ---
in line with the objectives of the EC Green Deal:

--- Document Chunk 3676 ---
Figure 1 – Sustainable mobility targets (Source: EC)

Annexes

--- Document Chunk 3832 ---
Environmental impacts of ERA activities

--- Document Chunk 3833 ---
ERA’s administrative operations related to its building(s) have direct and indirect impacts 

--- Document Chunk 3834 ---
on the environment. ERA’s impact on the environment falls under the following categories:

--- Document Chunk 3835 ---
1. Use of electricity, including for heating and cooling, water, paper and 

--- Document Chunk 3836 ---
stationery

--- Document Chunk 3837 ---
2. Generation of waste and CO2 emissions (including by travelling / com-

--- Document Chunk 3838 ---
muting)

--- Document Chunk 3839 ---
3. Land use with regards to biodiversity(73)

--- Document Chunk 3840 ---
ERA pays attention to limiting the use of resources, taking the energy crisis into account, 

--- Document Chunk 3841 ---
and minimising negative impacts on the environment.

--- Document Chunk 3842 ---
The recent geopolitical developments make the environmental – and in particular ener -

--- Document Chunk 3843 ---
gy-related issues – more visible than ever before.

--- Document Chunk 3844 ---
Accountability ceiling of ERA

--- Document Chunk 3845 ---
ERA is committed to do the utmost to advance its environment management and neutral-

--- Document Chunk 3846 ---
ise its impact on the environment. Nevertheless, it needs to be noted that due to outside 

--- Document Chunk 3847 ---
factors ERA’s leverage may be limited regarding some proposed environment actions.

--- Document Chunk 3848 ---
Current ERA headquarters building was put at the disposal of ERA by Valenciennes Métro-

--- Document Chunk 3849 ---
pole through a rental contract. Other buildings (meeting rooms in Lille, parking) used by 

--- Document Chunk 3850 ---
ERA are rented in office buildings and parking lots, where the environment management 

--- Document Chunk 3851 ---
responsibilities and tasks lie with the property owner or manager. In the context of the 

--- Document Chunk 3852 ---
Covid-19 pandemic, the Agency has re-assessed its approach to meetings with stakehold-

--- Document Chunk 3853 ---
ers and has limited the use of office spaces in Lille, as well as the missions of ERA staff and 

--- Document Chunk 3854 ---
externals to Lille headquarters. A large number of the Agency’s meetings have been held 

--- Document Chunk 3855 ---
in remote mode, thus reducing the carbon footprint.

--- Document Chunk 3856 ---
Moreover, ERA’s new headquarters building project has a key focus on environmental 

--- Document Chunk 3857 ---
considerations when setting up specifications and during negotiations. The new building 

--- Document Chunk 3858 ---
project complies with the EMAS/HQE recommendations.

--- Document Chunk 3859 ---
It has to be noted that the railway link with the adjacent Belgian city of Mons is missing for 

--- Document Chunk 3860 ---
decades, with no rail service on the section between Valenciennes and the Franco-Belgian 

--- Document Chunk 3861 ---
border. Despite recent plans brought back the hope for re-establishing the connection, as 

--- Document Chunk 3862 ---
of today this condition leaves no feasible public transportation option for the significant 

--- Document Chunk 3863 ---
proportion of ERA staff living in Belgium. ERA remains a vocal advocate of recommencing 

--- Document Chunk 3864 ---
cross-border railway operations as defined in its Strategic Statement 1  (74), with a particu-

--- Document Chunk 3865 ---
lar focus on this particular one. Nevertheless as of today, carbon footprint related to staff  

--- Document Chunk 3866 ---
commuting from Belgium to France needs to be mitigated with less desirable alternative 

--- Document Chunk 3867 ---
solutions, such as carpooling.

--- Document Chunk 3868 ---

--- Document Chunk 3869 ---

to	be	considered	for	significant	improvement	of	its	biodiversity.

--- Document Chunk 4228 ---
Building project in the planning phase

--- Document Chunk 4229 ---
Due to the growth of the Agency, the current building in Valenciennes does not offer any 

--- Document Chunk 4230 ---
longer the required conditions to accommodate staff and activities related to the Agen -

--- Document Chunk 4231 ---
cy’s role as railways’ Authority. Therefore, the Agency has re-allocated the majority of staff  

--- Document Chunk 4232 ---
members in double office spaces as a short-term solution. Another short-medium term 

--- Document Chunk 4233 ---
solution is the implementation of teleworking up to the limit set by the Management 

--- Document Chunk 4234 ---
Board Decision on Teleworking.

--- Document Chunk 4235 ---
In parallel, as part of a long-term solution, the Agency and Valenciennes Métropole have 

--- Document Chunk 4236 ---
started defining the requirements for a new building to accommodate ERA activities after 

--- Document Chunk 4237 ---
2028 by means of a Study composed of different phases. In 2018, the Phase I of the Study 

--- Document Chunk 4238 ---
confirmed that the current ERA HQ cannot accommodate all requirements related to the 

--- Document Chunk 4239 ---
Agency activities and growth.

--- Document Chunk 4240 ---
In 2019 and 2020, the Agency has managed to complete the Phases 2 and 4 of the tech-

--- Document Chunk 4241 ---
nical and functional study resulting in the approval of the technical specifications that will 

--- Document Chunk 4242 ---
be used as the base for the selection of architects in the Phase 3 of the Study.

--- Document Chunk 4243 ---
Taking into account the experience gained during the pandemic with large-scale tele -

--- Document Chunk 4244 ---
working and new ways of working, the building capacity was revised, and the technical 

--- Document Chunk 4245 ---
project adapted.

--- Document Chunk 4246 ---
The main objective for the Agency during 2021 was to prepare the technical and financial 

--- Document Chunk 4247 ---
dossier to be formally addressed to the EU Budgetary Authority for the approval of the 

--- Document Chunk 4248 ---
New ERA building project.

--- Document Chunk 4249 ---
In 2022, the Agency clarified with the DG MOVE, the EU Budgetary Authority, the steps 

--- Document Chunk 4250 ---
related to the procedure to be followed to have the project formally approved. On the 

--- Document Chunk 4251 ---
31/10/2022, a letter was sent to the EU Budgetary Authority with the file as part of the 

--- Document Chunk 4252 ---
Early information procedure under Article 266(2) of the Financial Regulation resulting in 

--- Document Chunk 4253 ---
the presentation on the 17/11/2022 of the ERA project to the Committee on Budgets in 

--- Document Chunk 4254 ---
Brussels, where it was noted that the file submitted by ERA was very comprehensive and 

--- Document Chunk 4255 ---
clear. Following the exchange of views held in the meeting of the Committee on Budgets, 

--- Document Chunk 4256 ---
some follow-up questions asked by Members during the discussion were sent to ERA. At 

--- Document Chunk 4257 ---
this stage, the EU Parliament confirmed that the procedure “Information préalable” can be 

--- Document Chunk 4258 ---
considered as closed.

--- Document Chunk 4259 ---
In 2023, Valenciennes Métropole decided to transfer the building project to the “Banque 

--- Document Chunk 4260 ---
des Territoires” that will launch the Call for Architects during Q4 2023 – Q1 2024 with the 

--- Document Chunk 4261 ---
purpose to be able to draft a Rental Lease Agreement proposal. This draft Lease Agree -

--- Document Chunk 4262 ---
ment will contain all the financial conditions needed by ERA to launch the formal pro -

--- Document Chunk 4263 ---
cedure (submission of the Final Technical and Financial Dossier) aiming at receiving the 

--- Document Chunk 4264 ---
approval of the Budgetary Authority for the ERA Building Project.
