Annex VIII. Privileges and immunities

--- Document Chunk 4274 ---
The Management Board approved the proposed Headquarters (or Seat) Agreement between the Agency and the host Member State without objections or negative votes in August 

--- Document Chunk 4275 ---
2018. (83) The Seat Agreement between the French Government and the Agency has been presented as draft legislation to the French National Assembly on 7 July 2021 (84) and has been 

--- Document Chunk 4276 ---
adopted and promulgated on 31 January 2022. The final text of the Seat Agreement can be found here (85). The following table presents the privileges granted to the Agency’s staff: (86)

--- Document Chunk 4277 ---

The Agency’s headquarters are located in Valenciennes and Lille. The French authority 

--- Document Chunk 4282 ---
pledge to provide the necessary support to ensure the location of the Agency’s 

--- Document Chunk 4283 ---
headquarters will remain unchanged. (Art. 3)

--- Document Chunk 4284 ---
The Agency’s premises are inviolable, exempt from perquisition, requisition, 

--- Document Chunk 4285 ---
confiscation or expropriation. No French authority can enter the building without 

--- Document Chunk 4286 ---

--- Document Chunk 4287 ---

--- Document Chunk 4288 ---
(Art. 4)

--- Document Chunk 4289 ---

--- Document Chunk 4290 ---
benefit from the same treatment the French Government provides to diplomatic 

--- Document Chunk 4291 ---
missions when it comes to official communication. No restriction can be placed on 

--- Document Chunk 4292 ---
neither official communication addressed to the Agency or a member of its personnel, 

--- Document Chunk 4293 ---

--- Document Chunk 4294 ---

--- Document Chunk 4295 ---
other official communications by courier or in sealed bags which shall be subject to 

--- Document Chunk 4296 ---

--- Document Chunk 4298 ---
(SNEs, experts, trainees, interims). (Art. 1).

EV ALUATIONS  | 107

--- Document Chunk 4363 ---
Annex IX. Evaluations

--- Document Chunk 4364 ---
The Agency has a system in place to monitor its performance and formalise an evaluation 

--- Document Chunk 4365 ---
of the results achieved in the year into the SPD dashboard, as an ongoing tool, as well 

--- Document Chunk 4366 ---
as through the Consolidated Annual Activity Report , which focuses on the achieve -

--- Document Chunk 4367 ---
ments of indicators and targets set out in the SPD.

--- Document Chunk 4368 ---
The following instruments are used for collecting the data and for triggering actions:

--- Document Chunk 4369 ---
  Work progress reports, filled in by projects and service managers reporting the 

--- Document Chunk 4370 ---
status of projects and services against the relevant plans, budget and human re -

--- Document Chunk 4371 ---
sources allocation, including SPD targets.

--- Document Chunk 4372 ---
  Budget execution monitoring, a continuous activity based on a daily automat-

--- Document Chunk 4373 ---
ed report fed with SUMMA data, displaying the level of appropriations, commit -

--- Document Chunk 4374 ---
ments and payments to date for each budget line and for each project/service

--- Document Chunk 4375 ---
  Monthly management monitoring reports, analysing and reviewing pro -

--- Document Chunk 4376 ---
ject and staff allocation (actuals vs planned), budget execution and risks/

--- Document Chunk 4377 ---
issues at project/service level

--- Document Chunk 4378 ---
  Monthly budget review meetings with the Management Team to analyse the 

--- Document Chunk 4379 ---
data from the budget execution monitoring and take timely decisions for deploy-

--- Document Chunk 4380 ---
ing / redeploying the resources. The redeployment of resources is brought to the 

--- Document Chunk 4381 ---
attention of the Management Board for information if the transfers are within one 

--- Document Chunk 4382 ---
title or between titles but below the 10% threshold or for decision if the transfers 

--- Document Chunk 4383 ---
are between titles and above the 10% threshold.

--- Document Chunk 4384 ---
  IMCS, part of the internal monitoring programme aimed at verifying that pro -

--- Document Chunk 4385 ---
cesses, projects, services and products comply with internal and external require -

--- Document Chunk 4386 ---
ments, including.

--- Document Chunk 4387 ---
  IAS audits

--- Document Chunk 4388 ---
  ECA audits

--- Document Chunk 4389 ---
  Non-Conformity register, where deviations from the relevant rules and provi -

--- Document Chunk 4390 ---
sions are recorded

--- Document Chunk 4391 ---
All the sources listed above allow the Agency governance bodies, namely the Manage -

--- Document Chunk 4392 ---
ment Team and the Management Board to monitor continuously the functioning of the 

--- Document Chunk 4393 ---
Agency. In order to allow this, the Agency has developed a performance dashboard 

--- Document Chunk 4394 ---
which is turning the data into meaningful information.

--- Document Chunk 4395 ---
The dashboard provides figures, charts and visuals about:

--- Document Chunk 4396 ---
  Human resources (incl. information on statutory staff members, geographical and 

--- Document Chunk 4397 ---
gender balance)

--- Document Chunk 4398 ---
  Budget management (Revenues and Expenditure, with a breakdown to budget 

--- Document Chunk 4399 ---
titles of budget envelope/appropriation and paid amounts to date)

--- Document Chunk 4400 ---
  Authority tasks (incl. the number of SSC/VA/TA applications received, number au -

--- Document Chunk 4401 ---
thorisations/certifications issued to date, planned and actual hours per authorisa -

--- Document Chunk 4402 ---
tion type)

--- Document Chunk 4403 ---
  Projects and services (incl. Budget and FTE planned vs. actual, status traffic lights 

--- Document Chunk 4404 ---
with information on red status, overall cost analysis)

--- Document Chunk 4405 ---
  Strengthening Action Plan (SAP) (recruitment status, SAP policy priorities, SAP 

--- Document Chunk 4406 ---
milestones, budget execution)

--- Document Chunk 4407 ---
  Audits (status on open recommendations)

--- Document Chunk 4410 ---
Terminology (87)

--- Document Chunk 4411 ---
The following terms are used in the SPD – in accordance with the Commission guideline 

--- Document Chunk 4412 ---
on evaluation:

--- Document Chunk 4413 ---
Strategic Statement (88) is a coherent area of action with objectives and resources. It is 

--- Document Chunk 4414 ---
the basic building block for the structure of the annual Work Programme, distinguishing 

--- Document Chunk 4415 ---
between operational activities – directly related to the mission and core tasks of the agen-

--- Document Chunk 4416 ---
cy, and horizontal/ cross-cutting activities – carried out to support operational activities 

--- Document Chunk 4417 ---
and staff.

--- Document Chunk 4418 ---
Objective describes what the agency wants to achieve either in the short or long term.

--- Document Chunk 4419 ---
Indicator is a characteristic or attribute that is measured regularly in order to assess to 

--- Document Chunk 4420 ---
what extent an objective has been met.

--- Document Chunk 4421 ---
Baseline is the point of reference against which achievement or progress towards objec-

--- Document Chunk 4422 ---
tives is measured.

--- Document Chunk 4423 ---
Milestone is an intermediate target set, expressed in quantitative or qualitative terms, 

--- Document Chunk 4424 ---
measuring progress towards the achievement of long-term objectives.

--- Document Chunk 4425 ---
Target is the ultimate desired situation, quantified and timed.

--- Document Chunk 4426 ---
Inputs are the human and financial resources used and the time required to produce 

--- Document Chunk 4427 ---
outputs.

--- Document Chunk 4428 ---
Actions are the work carried out over a certain period of time, consuming resources and 

--- Document Chunk 4429 ---
producing outputs in accordance with the objectives set.

--- Document Chunk 4430 ---
Outputs are what is directly produced or supplied through the agency intervention. They 

--- Document Chunk 4431 ---
often relate to the expected deliverables of the intervention and are identified based on 

--- Document Chunk 4432 ---
its operational objectives.

--- Document Chunk 4433 ---
Outcome is the envisaged medium to long term effects of a programme or policy out -

--- Document Chunk 4434 ---
put. While its results are not easily foreseeable and might not be entirely in the sphere of 

--- Document Chunk 4435 ---
control of the Agency, the outcome represents an intermediate medium-term step be -

--- Document Chunk 4436 ---
tween the agency’ outputs and longer-term societal impacts. The Agency has structured 

--- Document Chunk 4437 ---
its multiannual work programme according to desired outcomes to ensure all of its out -

--- Document Chunk 4438 ---
puts will contribute positively to its vision & ambition.

--- Document Chunk 4439 ---
Results are the direct effects of intervention(s) on the target groups.

--- Document Chunk 4440 ---
Impacts are the indirect or long-term effects of an intervention on the EU or global socie-

--- Document Chunk 4441 ---
ty that are, at least partly, expected to be influenced by agency’s interventions.

--- Document Chunk 4442 ---

--- Document Chunk 4443 ---
Article	70	of	the	Financial	Regulation	2018/1046	and	on	the	guidelines	for	the	SPD	and	the	CAAR,	C.	Terminology

--- Document Chunk 4444 ---
(88)	 Referred	to	as	“Activity”	in	former	SPDs

STRATEGy FOR THE ORGANISATIONAL  MANAGEMENT  AND INTERNAL  CONTROL  S ySTEMS | 109

--- Document Chunk 4446 ---
Annex X. Strategy for 

--- Document Chunk 4447 ---
the organisational 

--- Document Chunk 4448 ---
management and 

--- Document Chunk 4449 ---
internal control 

--- Document Chunk 4450 ---
systems

--- Document Chunk 4451 ---
The strategy gives an overview on how the internal control system is organised and is 

--- Document Chunk 4452 ---
contributing to the mitigation of the risks to the achievement of Agency’s objectives to 

--- Document Chunk 4453 ---
acceptable levels.

--- Document Chunk 4454 ---
The Agency is operating based on a management system designed to provide reasona -

--- Document Chunk 4455 ---
ble assurance regarding the achievement of the five internal control objectives derived 

--- Document Chunk 4456 ---
from the Agency’s Financial regulation as well as ensuring continuous improvement and 

--- Document Chunk 4457 ---
the need to implement a flexible and effective governance. The management system is 

--- Document Chunk 4458 ---
implemented through four high-level components (i) Strategic, (ii) Core, (iii) Support and 

--- Document Chunk 4459 ---
(iv) Measurement and improvement. Each component is including all 17 principles of the 

--- Document Chunk 4460 ---
Internal Control Framework (ICF). There is also a clear link with the internal components of 

--- Document Chunk 4461 ---
the ICF (i.e. control environment, risk assessment, control activities and monitoring). This 

--- Document Chunk 4462 ---
system is deployed further at the level of processes.

--- Document Chunk 4463 ---
The roles and responsibilities for implementing the system are integrated as follows:

--- Document Chunk 4464 ---
The Management Board represents the Member States, and the institutional stakehold-

--- Document Chunk 4465 ---
ers has a strategic role on budgetary and planning matters. It is overseeing the internal 

--- Document Chunk 4466 ---
controls and risk management of the Agency. It ensures that the Agency fulfils its mission 

--- Document Chunk 4467 ---
and performs the tasks assigned to it

--- Document Chunk 4468 ---
The Executive Director (ED) in its capacity of Authorising Officer (AO) and under the su-

--- Document Chunk 4469 ---
pervision of the Management Board is ultimately responsible for the management of the 

--- Document Chunk 4470 ---
internal control framework. The ED sets the tone at the tope and puts in place structures 

--- Document Chunk 4471 ---
and processes to gain reasonable assurance that the system is operating effectively.

--- Document Chunk 4472 ---
The heads of units/department in their capacity of/Authorising officer by delegation 

--- Document Chunk 4473 ---
(AOD) must ensure that the internal controls are efficient and effective in their area of re -

--- Document Chunk 4474 ---
sponsibility as per AO delegation of powers. Both AO and AOD in their capacity of process 

--- Document Chunk 4475 ---
owners are responsible for continuous improvement of the processes.

--- Document Chunk 4476 ---
The newly created function of manager in charge of Risk management and internal 

--- Document Chunk 4477 ---
control is fulfilled by a middle manager. It oversees the monitoring the implementation 

--- Document Chunk 4478 ---
of the internal control arrangements and for complete and accurate reporting on the op-

--- Document Chunk 4479 ---
eration and effectiveness of the internal control framework. This function is also in charge 

--- Document Chunk 4480 ---
of facilitating the risk management process.

--- Document Chunk 4481 ---
The accounting officer certifies the year-end accounts thus providing reasonable assur-

--- Document Chunk 4482 ---
ance that the accounts present a true and fair view of the financial situation of the Agency.

--- Document Chunk 4483 ---
All staff should ensure at their own level of competency that their activities comply with 

--- Document Chunk 4484 ---
rules and regulations and report any deficiency.

--- Document Chunk 4485 ---
The delegations of powers for executing the budget are detailed in internal procedures. 

--- Document Chunk 4486 ---
The implementation of the budget is done via projects and services which is reflected in 

--- Document Chunk 4487 ---
110 | SINGLE PROGRAMMING DOCUMENT 2024-2026

--- Document Chunk 4488 ---
Annexes

--- Document Chunk 4489 ---
empowering project and service managers in managing the associated risks and resourc-

--- Document Chunk 4490 ---
es without prejudice to the AO/AOD powers.

--- Document Chunk 4491 ---
The IAS is the internal auditor of the Agency and performs independent assessment on 

--- Document Chunk 4492 ---
the internal control systems based on a three-year plan. Complementary, internal audits 

--- Document Chunk 4493 ---
are performed. The external audit is performed by the European Court of Auditors (for the 

--- Document Chunk 4494 ---
legality and regularity of transactions) and an external company (for the accounts).

--- Document Chunk 4495 ---
Internal controls tools include:

--- Document Chunk 4496 ---
  Controls performed at all levels of the Agency

--- Document Chunk 4497 ---
  Risk management, in particular at project/service level and Agency level where 

--- Document Chunk 4498 ---
the most significant/relevant risks are captured including strategic risks (recorded 

--- Document Chunk 4499 ---
in the agency/corporate risk register and reported in the CAAR). Risks are formally 

--- Document Chunk 4500 ---
assessed at both inherent and residual level to make sure that the analysis of the 

--- Document Chunk 4501 ---
effectiveness of the controls in place is ensured before additional mitigating meas-

--- Document Chunk 4502 ---
ures are put in place (cost-effectiveness of controls).

--- Document Chunk 4503 ---
  Corrective/preventive measures are established when recurrent and systemic er -

--- Document Chunk 4504 ---
rors are recorded. Ex-ante nonconformities involving significant amount of money 

--- Document Chunk 4505 ---
(>15.000 euros) are approved by the AO

--- Document Chunk 4506 ---
  Internal control monitoring criteria for measuring the presence and the function -

--- Document Chunk 4507 ---
ing of the principles are in process of being developed considering the risk envi -

--- Document Chunk 4508 ---
ronment and are focused more on effectiveness and efficiency.

--- Document Chunk 4509 ---
  Follow-up of recommendations from ECA, IAS, Discharge authority as well as other 

--- Document Chunk 4510 ---
sources (e.g. external evaluations) to ensure that the actions plans are effectively 

--- Document Chunk 4511 ---
implemented within the agreed deadlines.

--- Document Chunk 4512 ---
  An integrated reporting system to inform and alert management on the progress 

--- Document Chunk 4513 ---
on the implementation of costs for each project/service as well as SPD outputs 

--- Document Chunk 4514 ---
(monthly dashboard). The cost data is connected to the source (SUMMA). It in -

--- Document Chunk 4515 ---
cludes several other parameters such as risks, issues, changes, corrective actions 

--- Document Chunk 4516 ---
taken, quality, milestones etc.

--- Document Chunk 4517 ---
  Budgetary status reports are produced on a daily basis including an overview 

--- Document Chunk 4518 ---
per unit of the budget execution per budget line for all fund sources, financial 

--- Document Chunk 4519 ---
information on commitments, payments and transfers, information on progress of 

--- Document Chunk 4520 ---
planned procurement and contracts. The information helps achieving the perfor -

--- Document Chunk 4521 ---
mance targets in these particular areas.

--- Document Chunk 4522 ---
  Ex-ante controls consisting in several checks of financial and operational aspects 

--- Document Chunk 4523 ---
of transactions by the actors involved in the financial circuits. There is a very com -

--- Document Chunk 4524 ---
prehensive checklist/templates as well as guidance which ensure an effective level 

--- Document Chunk 4525 ---
of control. The specific controls are detailed in the manual of financial procedures 

--- Document Chunk 4526 ---
which also included the steps to be taken for making a financial transaction, the 

--- Document Chunk 4527 ---
various financial circuits by type of transaction and the different roles and responsi-

--- Document Chunk 4528 ---
bilities. The Agency is putting substantial efforts in updated these manuals/check-

--- Document Chunk 4529 ---
lists.

--- Document Chunk 4530 ---
   Sensitive function policy defines the management of functions involving a consid-

--- Document Chunk 4531 ---
erable amount of autonomy and executive powers with the aim of ensuring that 

--- Document Chunk 4532 ---
actions are taken to mitigate the risk that the jobholders deliberately misuse their 

--- Document Chunk 4533 ---
decision-making powers or influence with a view to gaining personal advantages

--- Document Chunk 4534 ---
  Ad-hoc controls are additionally applied at the level of processes whenever the 

--- Document Chunk 4535 ---
management assesses it is necessary to mitigate a specific risk (e.g. selection pro -

--- Document Chunk 4536 ---
cedures, financial delegations).

--- Document Chunk 4537 ---
The Agency’s anti-fraud strategy has been developed in accordance with OLAF guidelines, 

--- Document Chunk 4538 ---
it is setting clear objectives, actions and responsibilities and it is based on a standalone 

--- Document Chunk 4539 ---
fraud risk assessment exercise adapted to the Agency’s environment encompassing fraud 

--- Document Chunk 4540 ---
STRATEGy FOR THE ORGANISATIONAL  MANAGEMENT  AND INTERNAL  CONTROL  S ySTEMS | 111

--- Document Chunk 4541 ---
risks regardless of their criticality. The risk of fraud is duly considered when carry out the 

--- Document Chunk 4542 ---
risk assessment exercise.

--- Document Chunk 4543 ---
The strategy is focusing on three objectives:

--- Document Chunk 4544 ---
  Handle effectively actual or perceived conflict of interest,

--- Document Chunk 4545 ---
  Enhance the promotion of high ethical values as well as increasing fraud aware -

--- Document Chunk 4546 ---
ness

--- Document Chunk 4547 ---
  Enhance data and information security

--- Document Chunk 4548 ---
The objectives are fully aligned with the fraud risks identified which include inherent sig -

--- Document Chunk 4549 ---
nificant risk of conflict of interest due to specific circumstances of the Agency’s activities 

--- Document Chunk 4550 ---
(i.e. regulatory powers with significant decision making powers and potential reputational, 

--- Document Chunk 4551 ---
legal and financial consequences if conflict of interest not adequately managed; relatively 

--- Document Chunk 4552 ---
limited ‘market’ for recruitment of staff as well as for entities which could provide services 

--- Document Chunk 4553 ---
for the Agency), potential risk of cyber-attacks leading to operational damage, loss of data, 

--- Document Chunk 4554 ---
unauthorised disclosure of information or breach of data; potential risk of outsourcing the 

--- Document Chunk 4555 ---
data and information security without proper security risk assessment), risk of staff mem -

--- Document Chunk 4556 ---
bers not being fully aware of their ethics obligations as well as handling and reporting 

--- Document Chunk 4557 ---
fraud. The Agency has put in place comprehensive control measures proportional to the 

--- Document Chunk 4558 ---
level of risks and amount of risk identified which encompass (but not limited to) manda -

--- Document Chunk 4559 ---
tory tailor-made trainings on ethics and separately on antifraud for all staff, mandatory 

--- Document Chunk 4560 ---
submission of declaration of interests for all staff and members of the Management Board 

--- Document Chunk 4561 ---
and of the Board of Appeal, ex-post/on the spot controls, review of internal procedures 

--- Document Chunk 4562 ---
(including procedures for reporting and handling fraud). Control indicators enable assess-

--- Document Chunk 4563 ---
ment of effectiveness of the measures taken.

--- Document Chunk 4564 ---
Starting 2023, the Agency is implementing the following activities under a single 

--- Document Chunk 4565 ---
service (Internal Management and Control System – ERA1158) to better support the 

--- Document Chunk 4566 ---
assurance function:

--- Document Chunk 4567 ---
1. 

--- Document Chunk 4568 ---
The internal management system coordination  – coordinating the proper imple -

--- Document Chunk 4569 ---
mentation of the internal control framework, ;

--- Document Chunk 4570 ---
2. The central financial verification;

--- Document Chunk 4571 ---
3. The contact point for IAS, ECA and EP discharge follow-up.

--- Document Chunk 4572 ---
Assessment of the effectiveness of the management system

--- Document Chunk 4573 ---
The agency monitors continuously the efficiency and effectiveness of the Internal Control 

--- Document Chunk 4574 ---
Framework. A yearly assessment report is produced where consideration is given to the 

--- Document Chunk 4575 ---
results of controls mentioned above. All the internal control components and principles 

--- Document Chunk 4576 ---
must be present and functioning well at all levels of the Agency to be considered effec-

--- Document Chunk 4577 ---
tive. The results of the assessment are reported in the CAAR.

--- Document Chunk 4848 ---
Annexes

--- Document Chunk 4849 ---
Annex XIV.  

--- Document Chunk 4850 ---
Strengthening Action 

--- Document Chunk 4851 ---
Plan (SAP) 2023-2027

--- Document Chunk 4852 ---
1. Context

--- Document Chunk 4853 ---
In 2022, the Agency’s Management Board adopted the Strengthening Plan prepared by 

--- Document Chunk 4854 ---
the Agency in close cooperation with the European Commission. The purpose of the 

--- Document Chunk 4855 ---
Strengthening Plan is to make the strongest possible case in order to strengthen the 

--- Document Chunk 4856 ---
Agency with resources matching the level of ambition necessary for achieving the 

--- Document Chunk 4857 ---
important EC policy objectives for rail, in an effective and efficient manner, and 

--- Document Chunk 4858 ---
benefit from high levels of ambition and efficiency within ERA’s structure and 

--- Document Chunk 4859 ---
methods.

--- Document Chunk 4860 ---
With the document serving as a basis for the internal EC budget negotiations in 2022, the 

--- Document Chunk 4861 ---
Agency received a proposed increase of 12 TAs in 2022  (92). While the additional TA allo -

--- Document Chunk 4862 ---
cation is lower compared to the request from the Strengthening Plan (12 TAs proposed 

--- Document Chunk 4863 ---
out of the 22 TAs requested), it can offer a good basis for the Agency to proceed with the 

--- Document Chunk 4864 ---
implementation of the Strengthening Plan.

--- Document Chunk 4865 ---
A very important challenge is represented by the fact that the additional TA allocation 

--- Document Chunk 4866 ---
needs to be fully covered under the existing subsidy envelope. To make best use of this 

--- Document Chunk 4867 ---
TA allocation and considering the external constraints related to the indexation of salaries 

--- Document Chunk 4868 ---
and prices, the Agency is making a thorough assessment of its capacity to cover these 

--- Document Chunk 4869 ---
costs in a sustainable manner until the end of MFF 2021-2027. Several measures are envis-

--- Document Chunk 4870 ---
aged, such as the time-phased hiring of the TAs. The budget constraint on the subsidy side 

--- Document Chunk 4871 ---
is therefore an element to be properly monitored and managed for the whole remaining 

--- Document Chunk 4872 ---
period of the current MFF.

--- Document Chunk 4873 ---
The current document describes the plan of actions which the Agency will put in place in 

--- Document Chunk 4874 ---
the period 2023-2027 in order to implement the Strengthening Plan, taking into consid -

--- Document Chunk 4875 ---
eration the level of additional staff allocation proposed by the EC. It is hereinafter referred 

--- Document Chunk 4876 ---
as SAP (Strengthening Action Plan) 2023-2027. This builds on actions already taken up to 

--- Document Chunk 4877 ---
present to increase the efficiency of the support services and tools.

--- Document Chunk 4878 ---
2. What we want to achieve

--- Document Chunk 4879 ---
ERA has established an outcome-driven framework, placing strong emphasis on effec -

--- Document Chunk 4880 ---
tiveness (i.e. “doing the right things”), in line with the prioritisation of activities included in 

--- Document Chunk 4881 ---
the Strengthening Plan. In parallel, a delivery structure based on Projects and Services has 

--- Document Chunk 4882 ---
been established. Outputs of projects and services are followed up and measured using a 

--- Document Chunk 4883 ---
dashboard approach.

--- Document Chunk 4884 ---
With the Strengthening Plan, we will implement a series of improvement actions that 

--- Document Chunk 4885 ---
should enable to achieve the most appropriate outcomes with the resources available. 

--- Document Chunk 4886 ---
This is important not only to justify the additional resources requested by the Agency, but 

--- Document Chunk 4887 ---
also in order to demonstrate that European taxpayer’s money is used in the most effective 

--- Document Chunk 4888 ---
way, so that the European railway system can develop towards attractiveness, efficiency, 

--- Document Chunk 4889 ---
and sustainability.

--- Document Chunk 4890 ---
(92)	 6	TAs	are	expected	to	be	phased	out	by	the	end	of	MFF	2021-2027

--- Document Chunk 4891 ---
STRENGTHENING  AC TION P LAN (SAP)  2023-2027  | 119

--- Document Chunk 4892 ---
Improvement actions will be assessed according to their impact as well as ease of imple -

--- Document Chunk 4893 ---
mentation. Quantitative targets are defined (mainly related to the respective FTEs) and fol-

--- Document Chunk 4894 ---
lowed up/measured on a regular basis. The baseline is ERA SPD 2022 and the monitoring 

--- Document Chunk 4895 ---
tools are ERA SPD Portfolio Management together with the SPD Dashboard developed 

--- Document Chunk 4896 ---
already.

--- Document Chunk 4897 ---
3. Objectives, actions, indicators, and targets

--- Document Chunk 4898 ---
The SAP 2023-2027 mirrors the Strengthening Plan and translated it into concrete actions. 

--- Document Chunk 4899 ---
It is based on the planning and monitoring framework and enablers already set up 

--- Document Chunk 4900 ---
by the Agency, which includes:

--- Document Chunk 4901 ---
  the multi-annual planning in the SPD, with a clear focus on the intervention logic;

--- Document Chunk 4902 ---
  the Agency’s performance dashboard, including reporting to the EB and the MB

--- Document Chunk 4903 ---
  the regular budget execution monitoring and reporting

--- Document Chunk 4904 ---
  the Consolidated Annual Activity Report.

--- Document Chunk 4905 ---
The annual work programmes will therefore be aligned to the priorities listed in the SAP , 

--- Document Chunk 4906 ---
which represents an anchor for the multi-annual planning in what the priority policy areas 

--- Document Chunk 4907 ---
are concerned. A direct tracking of SAP-related FTEs, outputs and targets will be includes 

--- Document Chunk 4908 ---
in the SPDs.

--- Document Chunk 4909 ---
The SAP 2023-2027 is organised along the following components/objectives:

--- Document Chunk 4910 ---
a.)  Drive an optimal resourcing of policy priority areas, matched by proportional out-

--- Document Chunk 4911 ---
puts and outcomes, including efficiency gains

--- Document Chunk 4912 ---
b.)  Maintain proper resourcing and further efficiency gains for the authority tasks

--- Document Chunk 4913 ---
c.)  Ensure a reduction in the Agency’s administrative FTE allocation while maintaining 

--- Document Chunk 4914 ---
regularity and legality

--- Document Chunk 4915 ---
d.)  Ensure the overall projected FTE evolution by 2027

--- Document Chunk 4916 ---
e.)  Ensure effective and efficient budget management (planning and execution), ap -

--- Document Chunk 4917 ---
propriate risk management

--- Document Chunk 4918 ---

--- Document Chunk 5454 ---
C. Ensure a re duction in the Agency’s administrative FTE allocation

--- Document Chunk 5455 ---
Note 1: This objective is referred to the administrative FTE allocation, but encompasses a wide scope (e.g. redeploying administrative posts to operational activities, redeploying technical staff who 

--- Document Chunk 5456 ---
currently cover administrative tasks to operational tasks activities).

--- Document Chunk 5457 ---
All references are to FTEs (not posts) to allow for counting savings and/or redeployments which account for partitions of one FTE.

--- Document Chunk 5458 ---
Note 2: The sequencing is thought as follows:

--- Document Chunk 5459 ---
i.  Creating the capacity of potentially free FTEs through process leaning, including automation – as such, this does not account for a materialised saving, but is a pre-condition (step 

--- Document Chunk 5460 ---
C2)

--- Document Chunk 5461 ---
ii.  Identifying the opportunities to materialise that capacity – this can happen at contract end points (step C3)

--- Document Chunk 5462 ---
iii.  Having the FTEs freed from administrative work needs to be followed up by their actual redeployment in operational areas (step C4)

--- Document Chunk 5463 ---
(105)	 This	reflects	the	re-visited	assumptions	for	the	use	of	ERA	FTEs	for	VA,	SSC,	ERTMS	TA	compared	to	2022	and	also	embeds	a	component	of	efficiency	gains	through	simplification/automation	of	processes.

STRENGTHENING  AC TION P LAN (SAP)  2023-2027  | 131

--- Document Chunk 5655 ---
Budget related

--- Document Chunk 5656 ---
Risk Risk 

--- Document Chunk 5657 ---
assessment Mitigating measures

--- Document Chunk 5658 ---
1. The Agency might not be in the position to hire all 12 TAs in 2023 due to subsidy 

--- Document Chunk 5659 ---
constraints. The inflation trend poses significant pressure on the Agency’s capacity to 

--- Document Chunk 5660 ---
cover the salary costs in the absence of sufficient additional EU subsidy.

--- Document Chunk 5661 ---
4

--- Document Chunk 5662 ---
The Agency is carefully monitoring the budget execution to strike the optimal use of 

--- Document Chunk 5663 ---
the existing resources in the spirit of sound financial management, while flagging early 

--- Document Chunk 5664 ---
warning signals in case of subsidy gaps. We will react by an agile approach, having 

--- Document Chunk 5665 ---
reserve lists in place but only conclude employment contracts when the budgetary 

--- Document Chunk 5666 ---
means are available.

--- Document Chunk 5667 ---
2. The revenues from Fees and Charges are not under the full control of the Agency. 

--- Document Chunk 5668 ---
In particular, the volume of work can fluctuate due to seasonal trends during the year, 

--- Document Chunk 5669 ---
but also more structurally, upwards (e.g. the need for re-certification following DAC 

--- Document Chunk 5670 ---
deployment, go-everywhere trains etc.) or downwards (e.g. starting with the second 

--- Document Chunk 5671 ---
round of safety certification for the same RU at ERA, the complexity of the issues and 

--- Document Chunk 5672 ---
checks might drop compared to the first round).

--- Document Chunk 5673 ---
4

--- Document Chunk 5674 ---
Human resources and internal communication related

--- Document Chunk 5675 ---
Risk Risk 

--- Document Chunk 5676 ---
assessment Mitigating measures

--- Document Chunk 5677 ---
3. The changes in the working patterns, together with the financial consideration for 

--- Document Chunk 5678 ---
hiring at lower grades, might limit the attractiveness for the specialised technical jobs 

--- Document Chunk 5679 ---
offered by the Agency in the future. This might hamper the business continuity, talent 

--- Document Chunk 5680 ---
pool retention and by consequence, Agency’s capacity to deliver the technical outputs 

--- Document Chunk 5681 ---
envisaged in this plan.

--- Document Chunk 5682 ---
3

--- Document Chunk 5683 ---
4. Inherent internal communication sensitivity around the choices made as part of 

--- Document Chunk 5684 ---
the action plan (non-replacement, redeployment etc.). In addition, given this internal 

--- Document Chunk 5685 ---
redeployment, the pressure on legally binding administrative tasks will increase 

--- Document Chunk 5686 ---
exponentially.

--- Document Chunk 5687 ---
4

--- Document Chunk 5688 ---
The Agency will indeed tackle this aspect with attention, by highlighting and 

--- Document Chunk 5689 ---
supporting the opportunity of ensuring career paths from administrative tasks to 

--- Document Chunk 5690 ---
operational tasks. Natural end-of-contract gate reviews will be used.
